قوله : (وحد بوطء أمة أخيه وعمه وإن ظن حله وامرأة وجدت في فراشه) يعني سواء ظن الحل أو الحرمة لأنه لا انبساط في الأخ والعم وكذا سائر المحارم سوى الولاد لما بينا ولا اشتباه في المرأة الموجودة على فراشه لطول الصحبة فلم يكن مستنداً إلى دليل، وهذا لأنه قد ينام على فراشه غيرها من المحارم التي في بيتها . أطلقه فشمل البصير والأعمى لأنه يمكنه التمييز بالسؤال وغيره إلا إذا دعاها فأجابته وقالت أنا زوجتك أو أنا فلانة باسم زوجته فواقعها لأن الإخبار دليل. وفي التبيين : وإن جاءت بولد يثبت نسبه لما نذكره في المرقوقة ولو أجابته فقط يحد لعدم ما السقوط. وأطلق في المرأة فشمل المكرهة والطائعة فيحد لو أكرهها دونها ولا يجب المهر عندنا قوله : (لا بأجنبية زفت وقيل هي زوجتك) أي لا يحد بوطء أجنبية زفت إليه وقال النساء هي زوجتك، قضى بذلك علي رضي الله عنه، ولأنه اعتمد دليلاً وهو الإخبار في موضع الاشتباه إذ الإنسان لا يميز بين امرأة وبين غيرها في أول الوهلة فصار كالمغرور ولكن لا يحد قاذفه لأن الملك منعدم حقيقة فبطل به إحصانه كوطء جارية ابنه فإنه مسقط لإحصانه حبلت أو لا. وظاهر كلام المصنف أن إخبار واحدة له بأنها زوجته يكفي لإسقاط الحد عنه كما يفيده ما في فتح القدير لكن عبارة القدوري وقلن النساء بالجمع والظاهر أنه ليس بشرط سنبينه لأنه من المعاملات والواحد فيها يكفي اهـ.
His statement: (And he is subject to hadd by intercourse with the slave-girl of his brother and his uncle, even if he thought it halal, and a woman found in his bed.) Meaning: whether he thought it halal or forbidden, because there is no [allowance for] expansion in the brother and uncle, and likewise the rest of the mahrams except through lineage as we explained, and there is no confusion regarding the woman found on his bed due to long companionship, so it is not based on evidence. This is because beside him [in bed] may sleep other mahrams who are in his house. He [the text] made it unrestricted, so it includes the sighted and the blind, because he can distinguish by asking or otherwise; except if he called her and she answered and said 'I am your wife' or 'I am so-and-so' by his wife's name, and he had intercourse with her, because the report is evidence. In al-Tabyeen: And if she brings a child, his lineage is established, as we will mention in the case of the woman who is 'mazzufa' (brought as bride). And if she merely answered, he is subject to hadd due to the lack of [grounds for] dropping it. And he [the text] made it unrestricted regarding the woman, so it includes both the coerced and the willing; he is subject to hadd if he coerces her, but no mahr is due according to us. His statement: (Not by an outsider woman who is brought as bride and it is said she is your wife.) i.e., he is not subject to hadd by intercourse with an outsider woman who is brought to him and women say she is his wife. 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) gave judgment accordingly, and because he relied on evidence, i.e., the report, in a place of confusion, since a person cannot distinguish between a woman and another at the first glance, so he becomes like one deceived. But his slanderer is not subject to hadd because ownership is non-existent in reality, so his ihsan is nullified, like intercourse with his son's slave-girl, for it nullifies his ihsan whether she becomes pregnant or not. The apparent meaning of the author's words is that the report of one woman to him that she is his wife suffices to drop the hadd, as is understood from Fath al-Qadir; but the wording of al-Quduri is 'and women said' in the plural. And the apparent is that it is not a condition; we will clarify it because it is from mu'amalat (transactions) and one suffices in them.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's statement about hadd for intercourse with a brother's or uncle's slave-girl, or a woman found in one's bed. The commentator explains that hadd is wajib in these cases regardless of whether the person thought it halal or not. The reason is that there is no implicit permission (inbisat) with a brother or uncle to have access to their slave-girls, nor is there confusion about a woman found on one's own bed due to long association (the man knows who sleeps in his bed). This ruling applies to both sighted and blind men, because they can ask and ascertain. However, if the man calls a woman and she responds saying she is his wife (or calls herself by his wife's name), then hadd is dropped because he relied on her report as evidence. If she merely responds without such words, hadd remains. The text also considers whether the woman is coerced or willing; if he coerces her, he still faces hadd but no mahr (since the mahr is not due in zina according to the Hanafis). Then the commentary moves to the exception: an ajnabiyya (a woman not his wife) who is brought to him as a bride (zuffat) and women say she is his wife; in this case, hadd is dropped because he relied on evidence (the women's report) in a situation of confusion. This was the judgment of 'Ali (RA). The man is like a deceived person (maghrur). However, his qadhif (slanderer) is not punished because there is no actual marriage, but the man's ihsan (which enables hadd for slander) is nullified by this intercourse. The commentator also clarifies that according to the author of al-Hidayah, the report of a single woman suffices to drop hadd, even though al-Quduri mentioned 'women' in the plural, but that is not a condition because it is a transactional matter where one witness suffices.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed, divinely ordained punishment for specific offenses, such as zina (adultery/fornication).
المحارم (al-maharim): Those who are permanently forbidden for marriage due to blood, marriage, or fosterage.
المغرور (al-maghrur): A person who is deceived into doing something; here, a man who is told a woman is his wife and acts upon that.
الشبهة (al-shubha): A legal doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of the fixed punishment (hadd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is hadd not imposed for intercourse with a woman found in one's bed?
A) If the man is blind.
B) If the woman calls herself by the man's wife's name when he calls her.
C) If the man thought it was halal.
D) If the woman was coerced.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for unlawful intercourse is dropped only when the man relies on credible external evidence, such as the woman's own report, creating a valid shubha.

Mahr Obligation When Hadd Drops Due to Shubha
Expansion of the mahr obligation rule and its exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that mahr al-mithl is wajib when hadd drops due to shubha, identify the exceptions (e.g., son's slave-girl, seller's case), and explain the intra-madhhab dispute on whether mere zifaf constitutes a shubha.

Core Idea
When hadd drops due to shubha, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib — with specific exceptions.

In Hanafi fiqh, any consensual intercourse in Dar al-Islam must have a legal consequence: either the hadd punishment or a financial obligation (mahr). When the hadd is dropped because of a shubha (doubt), the mahr becomes due to preserve the dignity of the woman. This lesson unpacks the rule, its exceptions, and a key internal debate: is the mere act of a bride being brought to the husband (zifaf) sufficient to create a shubha, or is an explicit report required?

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Start with the foundational statement: any intercourse in Dar al-Islam either imposes hadd or necessitates mahr. This is the basis for the entire ruling.
2
Understand When Hadd Drops, Mahr Becomes Wajib
When hadd is dropped due to shubha, the mahr obligation crystallizes. The mahr is mahr al-mithl (the standard bridewealth), as ruled by 'Ali (RA).
This applies to all shubha cases except those specifically excluded.
3
Recognize the Exceptions
Learn the exceptions: intercourse with one's own slave-girl (master owes no debt to slave), with the son's slave-girl (if he claims paternity), and the seller's intercourse with the sold item before delivery. In these cases, mahr is not obligatory.
Also note the rule does not apply when the woman forfeits her right (e.g., prepubescent boy case).
4
Analyze the Dispute: Zifaf as Shubha
Some Hanafis require an explicit report that she is the wife; others (preferred by the commentator) hold that mere zifaf (the act of bringing the bride) suffices as a strong shubha. The latter view is based on custom, avoiding hardship, and the precedent of 'Ali (RA).
This dispute affects whether hadd can be imposed in the absence of a report.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وعليه مهر بذلك قضى علي رضي الله عنه وبالعدة لأن الوطء في دار الإسلام لا يخلو عن الحد أو المهر وقد سقط الحد فتعين المهر وهو مهر المثل، ولهذا قلنا في كل سقط فيه الحد مما ذكرنا يجب فيه المهر لما ذكرنا إلا في وطء جارية الابن وقد علقت منه وادعى نسبه لما ذكرنا في النكاح أو في وطء البائع المبيعة قبل التسليم؛ ذكرها في الزيادات. وينبغي أن لا يجب بوطء جارية السيد لأن المولى لا يجب له دين على عبده، ولو قيل وجب ثم سقط فمستقيم على ما اختلفوا في تزويج المولى عبده بجاريته ؛ كذا في التبيين. ولا يرد ما لو زنى صبي بامرأة بالغة مطاوعة قالوا لا حد على الصبي ولا مهر عليه لإسقاطها حقها حيث مكنته لأن المهر وجب لكنه سقط لما ذكرنا فلم يخل وطء عنهما. وفي المجتبى : مراهق تزوج بالغة بغير إذن أبيه ووطئها ورد الأب النكاح فلا مهر على الصبي لأن قوله غير معتبر. وأراد المصنف أن يكون المهر لها عليه بذلك قضى علي رضي الله عنه خلافاً لعمر رضي الله عنه حيث جعله في بيت المال كأنه جعله حق الشرع لما أن الحد حق له وهذا النسب قوله : (وظاهر كلام المصنف الخ أقول : ظاهر هذا أنه لا بد من الإخبار وأنه لا يكفي مجرد زفافها إليه لكن عبارة الحاكم الشهيد في الكافي تفيد عدم اشتراطه حيث قال : رجل تزوج امرأة فزفت إليه أخرى فوطئها قال : لا حد عليه ولا على قاذفه ثم علله بأن الزفاف شبهة ولذا لو جاءت بولد ثبت نسبه منه .اهـ. فجعل الشبهة نفس الزفاف، ولعل هذا رواية أخرى وعليها مشى في الخانية أيضاً، ويكون ما في المتون رواية غيرها وينبغي على الثانية أن من زفت إليه زوجته ولم يكن رآها أنه لا يحل له وطؤها ما لم تقل له النساء هذه زوجتك لاحتمال أنها تكون غيرها وفي ذلك حرج فإنه لا يكاد أحد يفعله الآن فيلزم تأثيم الناس على أن احتمال كونها غيرها احتمال ضعيف ربما لا يقع في سنين عديدة إلا نادراً أو لا سيما إذا كانت في بيته ليلة الزفاف واجتمع عليها أهله وأقاربه وغيرهن وزينوها وأفردوها في محل مخصوص ثم أدخلت عليه، فإن احتمال كونها غيرها أبعد ما يكون فوجوب السؤال بعيد أيضاً والظاهر أنه يكفي مجرد زفافها عملاً بهذا الظاهر بل هو أقوى مما لو جاءت بها امرأة من بيت أهلها ثم أدخلتها عليه وقالت له هذه زوجتك فإنه يحتمل كذبها
His statement: (And upon him is the mahr thereby; 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) gave judgment accordingly, and the 'idda.) Because intercourse in the Abode of Islam is never free from either hadd or mahr; when hadd has dropped, mahr becomes incumbent, and it is mahr al-mithl. For this reason we have said that in every case where we mentioned that hadd dropped, mahr is obligatory, except in the case of intercourse with the son's slave-girl when she conceived from him and he claimed lineage, as we mentioned in the chapter on marriage, or in the case of the seller's intercourse with the sold item before delivery; it is mentioned in al-Ziyadat. And it should be that it is not obligatory by intercourse with the master's slave-girl, because a debt is not due from a slave to his master. And if it is said that it is obligatory then drops, it is plausible, based on their disagreement on the marriage of a master marrying his slave to his slave-girl. Similarly in al-Tabyeen. And it does not contradict [the rule] that if a prepubescent boy commits adultery with a compliant adult woman, they said: there is no hadd on the boy and no mahr upon him, because she forfeited her right by enabling him. For the mahr was obligatory but dropped for the reason mentioned, so the intercourse was not free from both. In al-Mujtaba: A youth (murahiq) married an adult without his father's permission, had intercourse, and the father annulled the marriage; then no mahr is due from the boy because his statement is not valid. And the author intended that the mahr is for her from him; 'Ali (RA) gave judgment accordingly, contrary to 'Umar (RA) who placed it in the public treasury (bayt al-mal) as if he considered it a right of Allah, because the hadd is His right. And his statement: (And the apparent meaning of the author's words, etc.) I say: The apparent meaning is that there must be a report, and mere bringing of the bride (zifaf) does not suffice. But the wording of al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Kafi indicates that it is not a condition, where he said: A man married a woman, then another was brought to him as a bride and he had intercourse with her. He said: There is no hadd on him and no [hadd] on his slanderer. Then he justified it by saying that the zifaf is a shubha, and for that reason, if she brings a child, his lineage is established from him. So he made the shubha the very zifaf. Perhaps this is another narration, and according to it, he proceeded in al-Khaniyya as well. And what is in the texts is a different narration. And it follows from the second view that if a man's wife is brought to him as a bride and he had not seen her, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her unless women tell him 'This is your wife', because she might be another woman. And that involves hardship, for hardly anyone would do that nowadays, and it would lead to sinning of the people. Moreover, the probability that she is another is weak, perhaps not occurring in many years except rarely, especially if she is in his house on the wedding night, with his family and relatives gathering and adorning her, and they put her in a specific place, then she is brought to him. The probability that she is another is most remote. Therefore, the obligation of asking is also remote. The apparent view is that mere zifaf suffices, acting on this apparent [circumstance]. In fact, it is stronger than if a woman from her family brings her and enters her upon him and says to him 'This is your wife', because she could be lying.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the ajnabiyya case and the consequences of hadd dropping. The commentator explains the general principle: in dar al-Islam, any intercourse either incurs hadd or necessitates mahr. When hadd is dropped due to shubha, mahr (specifically mahr al-mithl, the standard bridewealth) becomes obligatory. This applies to all the cases of shubha mentioned earlier, with two exceptions: (1) intercourse with one's son's slave-girl if she becomes pregnant and he claims the child; (2) the seller's intercourse with the sold item before delivery (mentioned in al-Ziyadat). Also, mahr is not obligatory for intercourse with one's own slave-girl because a master does not owe his slave. The commentator addresses a potential objection: if a prepubescent boy commits zina with a willing adult woman, there is no hadd on the boy and no mahr because the woman forfeited her right by enabling him. But this is not a counterexample because the mahr was initially obligatory but dropped due to her action. Similarly, a youth who marries without permission and then the father annuls it does not owe mahr because his statement is invalid. The passage then returns to the earlier dispute: the author of al-Kafi (al-Hakim al-Shahid) holds that mere zifaf (the woman being brought to the man as a bride) is a shubha sufficient to drop hadd, even without explicit report from women. This is supported by the judgment of 'Ali (RA). The commentator prefers this view, arguing that the probability of a stranger being mistaken for the bride is extremely weak, especially in the context of a wedding with family and preparations. Therefore, requiring explicit confirmation (like women saying 'this is your wife') would impose hardship and is unnecessary. The prevailing view in the madhhab is that mere zifaf suffices to create shubha, dropping hadd and establishing mahr and even lineage if a child is born.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard bridewealth for a woman of similar status to the one with whom intercourse occurred.
الزفاف (al-zifaf): The act of bringing a bride to the husband's home; here, it is considered a shubha that can drop hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what suffices to drop hadd and necessitate mahr in the case of an ajnabiyya brought as a bride?
A) Only if multiple women testify that she is his wife.
B) Only if the man asks and she verbally confirms.
C) Mere zifaf (the act of her being brought as a bride) is sufficient.
D) Only if the man has seen her before.

Key Takeaway
When hadd drops due to shubha, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib to the woman, and mere zifaf is sufficient as a shubha according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Marriage to a Mahram and the Hadd Penalty: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadd for marrying a mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether the hadd of zina applies to a man who marries a mahram, and explain the conceptual basis of their disagreement regarding the 'mahall' of the contract.

Core Idea
The hadd drops only if the contract creates shubha; Abu Hanifa sees shubha in the mahall's purpose, the Sahibayn see none.

This lesson tackles an intra-Hanafi dispute on the application of the hadd penalty when a man knowingly marries a permanently prohibited woman (mahram) and consummates the marriage. The disagreement hinges on the definition of the 'proper place' (mahall) of the marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is a man marrying a mahram (e.g., his sister) and having intercourse with her. The disputed ruling is whether the hadd of zina applies.
The hadd is the fixed punishment for unlawful intercourse.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that no hadd applies due to shubha. His proof: the contract encountered its proper place (mahall) because the woman is capable of procreation, which is the purpose of marriage. Though the contract fails to yield permissibility, it creates a shubha that drops the hadd.
Shubha here is a legal ambiguity that precludes punishment.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the hadd applies if the man knew the prohibition. Their proof: the contract did not encounter its proper place because the mahall must accept the ruling of permissibility, and a mahram is never permissible. Thus the contract is void and no shubha exists.
The Sahibayn define the mahall in terms of the ruling (hukm), not the purpose.
4
Analyze the point of contention: definition of mahall
The core disagreement is whether the 'mahall' of a marriage contract is defined by its purpose (procreation) or its ruling (permissibility). Abu Hanifa takes the former view; the Sahibayn the latter. This determines the presence of shubha.
The text notes that they are not talking about the same 'mahall' – one considers the contract generically, the other specifies it to this particular contract.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the practical consequence
The fatwa is on the opinion of the Sahibayn, as stated in al-Khulasa and adopted by Abu al-Layth. Thus the operative ruling: hadd is applied if the man knew the prohibition. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the hadd is executed or not.
The marriage is invalid in all cases; only the punishment differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وبمحرم (نكحها أي لا يجب الحد بوطء امرأة محرم له عقد عليها عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : عليه الحد إذا كان عالماً بذلك لأنه عقد لم يصادف محله فيلغو كما إذا أضيف إلى الذكور. وهذا لأن محل التصرف ما يكون محلاً لحكمه وحكمه في الحل وهي من المحرمات. ولأبي حنيفة أن العقد صادف محله لأن محل التصرف ما يقبل مقصوده والأنثى من بنات آدم قابلة للتوالد وهو المقصود وكان ينبغي أن ينعقد في حق جميع الأحكام إلا أنه تقاعد عن إفادة حقيقة الحل فيورث الشبهة لأن الشبهة ما بشبه الثابت لا نفس الثابت. وحاصل الخلاف أن هذا العقد هل يوجب شبهة أم لا، ومداره أنه هل ورده على ما محله أو لا؟ هو فعند الإمام ورد على ما هو محله لأن المحلية ليست بقبول الحل بل بقبول مقاصد العقد من وهو ثابت ولذا صح من غيره عليها وعندهما لا لأن محل العقد ما يقبل حكمه وحكمه الحل وهذه من المحرمات في سائر الأحوال فكان الثابت صورة العقد لانعقاده، وبتأمل يظهر أنهم لم يتواردوا على محل واحد في المحلية فحيث نفوا محليتها أرادوا بالنسبة إلى خصوص هذا العاقد أي ليست محلاً لعقد هذا العاقد، ولهذا عللوه بعدم حلها، ولا شك في حلها لغيره بعقد النكاح لا محليتها للعقد من حيث هو والإمام حيث أثبت محليتها أراد محليتها لنفس العقد لا بالنظر إلى خصوص عاقد ولذا علل بقبولها مقاصده ولا ينافيه قول الأصوليين أن النهي يسير في بيت المال. قوله : ( وفي فتح القدير والأوجه الخ) أقول : ذكر في الفتح بعد هذا بأسطر ما نصه : والحاصل أنه لو اعتبر شبهة اشتباه أشكل عليه ثبوت النسب، وأطلقوا أن فيها لا يثبت النسب وإن اعتبر شبهة محل اقتضى أنه لو قال علمتها حراماً علي لعلمي بكذب النساء لا يحد، ويحد قاذفه . والحق أنه شبهة اشتباه لانعدام الملك من كل وجه وكون الإخبار يطلق الجماع شرعاً ليس هو الدليل المعتبر في شبهة المحل لأن الدليل المعتبر فيه هو ما مقتضاه ثبوت الملك نحو «أنت ومالك لأبيك» والملك القائم للشريك لا ما يطلق شرعاً مجرد الفعل غير أنه يستثنى من الحكم المرتب عليه أعني عدم ثبوت النسب للإجماع فيه، وبهذه والمعتدة ظهر عدم انضباط ما مهدوه من أحكام الشبهتين اهـ. وعلى هذا مشى المؤلف أولاً فكان عليه أن يذكر كلام الفتح هذا ولا يقتصر على ما ذكره . ثم قال: عن نكاح المحارم مجاز عن النفي لعدم محله ولا قول الفقهاء أن محل النكاح الأنثى من بنات آدم التي ليست من المحرمات لأنهم أرادوا نفي المحلية لعقد النكاح الخاص، وأنت علمت أن أبا حنيفة إنما أثبت محليتها للنكاح في الجملة لا بالنظر إلى خصوص ناكح لكن قد أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث بقولهما قال في الواقعات ونحن نأخذ به أيضاً. وفي الخلاصة: الفتوى على قولهما. ووجه ترجيحه أن تحقق الشبهة يقتضي تحقق الحل من وجه لأن الشبهة لا محالة شبهة الحل لكن حلها ليس ثابتاً من وجه وإلا وجبت العدة وثبت النسب أطلق المصنف فشمل ما إذا كان عالماً بالحرمة أو لا .
His statement: (And by a mahram he married her) meaning that hadd is not obligatory for intercourse with a woman who is a mahram to him if he contracted marriage with her according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said: The hadd is upon him if he knew that, because it is a contract that did not encounter its proper place, so it is invalid, just as if it were added to males. And this is because the place of a disposition is that which is a place for its ruling, and its ruling is permissibility, and she is among the prohibited women. And for Abu Hanifa, the contract encountered its proper place because the place of a disposition is that which accepts its purpose, and the female of the daughters of Adam is capable of procreation, which is the purpose, and it should be concluded regarding all rulings except that it fell short of yielding true permissibility, so it creates shubha because shubha is what resembles the established, not the established itself. The summary of the disagreement is whether this contract creates shubha or not, and its pivot is whether it occurred upon its proper place or not. According to the Imam, it occurred upon its proper place because locality is not acceptance of permissibility but acceptance of the purposes of the contract, which are established, and therefore it is valid from others upon her. According to the two, it is not because the place of the contract is that which accepts its ruling, and its ruling is permissibility, and she is among the prohibited women in all circumstances, so what is established is the form of the contract due to its conclusion. Upon reflection, it appears that they did not converge on one place regarding locality. When they negate locality, they mean with respect to this particular contractor, i.e., she is not a place for the contract of this contractor, and for this reason they reasoned it with her lack of permissibility. There is no doubt that she is permissible for others by a marriage contract, not her locality for the contract as such. The Imam, when he affirmed locality, meant locality for the contract itself, not with respect to a particular contractor, and for this he reasoned by her acceptance of its purposes, and it is not contradicted by the statement of the usuliyyun that the prohibition is easy in the treasury of the state. His statement: (And in Fath al-Qadir, the most likely opinion etc.) I say: He mentioned in al-Fath after this by a few lines: The result is that if shubha of confusion were considered, the establishment of nasab would be problematic, and they stated that in it, nasab is not established. And if shubha of the place were considered, it would require that if he said 'I know she is forbidden to me due to my knowledge of the women's lying', he would not be hadded, and his slanderer would be hadded. The truth is that it is shubha of confusion due to the absence of ownership from every aspect, and the fact that the report permits intercourse legally is not the evidence considered in shubha of the place, because the evidence considered there is that which mandates the establishment of ownership, like 'you and your property belong to your father' and the existing ownership of a partner, not what legally permits a mere act. However, it is exempted from the ruling built upon it, namely the non-establishment of nasab due to consensus on it, and with this and the waiting period, the lack of precision in what they laid down of the rulings of the two shubhas becomes apparent. End. And upon this the author proceeded initially, so it was incumbent upon him to mention this statement of al-Fath and not confine himself to what he mentioned. Then he said: Regarding marriage to maharim, it is a metaphor for negation due to the absence of its place, and there is no statement of the jurists that the place of marriage is a female of the daughters of Adam who is not among the prohibited women, because they intended to negate the locality for a specific marriage contract. And you know that Abu Hanifa affirmed her locality for marriage in general, not with respect to a particular husband. But the jurist Abu al-Layth adopted the opinion of the two, saying in al-Waqi'at: We also adopt it. And in al-Khulasa: The fatwa is on the opinion of the two. And the reason for its preference is that the realization of shubha requires the realization of permissibility from some aspect, because shubha is inevitably a shubha of permissibility, but its permissibility is not established from one aspect, otherwise 'idda would be obligatory and nasab would be established. The author made it absolute, so it includes whether he knew of the prohibition or not.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a man who marries a mahram (a woman prohibited for marriage due to blood relation, suckling, or affinity) incurs the hadd penalty for zina if he has intercourse with her. The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that no hadd is required if he marries a mahram. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains the positions. Abu Hanifa holds that although the marriage is invalid, the contract is not entirely void; it creates a shubha (legal ambiguity) because the female is capable of procreation, which is the purpose of marriage. Therefore, the hadd is dropped due to shubha. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the contract is void ab initio because it did not encounter a proper subject (mahall) since the woman is not capable of being a wife to this man due to her prohibition. Thus, if he knows the prohibition, the hadd applies. The dispute centers on the nature of the mahall (subject of the contract): Abu Hanifa defines it as that which accepts the purpose of the contract (procreation), while the Sahibayn define it as that which accepts the ruling (permissibility). The Sahibayn's view is adopted as the fatwa (mufta bihi) according to al-Khulasa, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi also followed it. The text also discusses the difference between shubha of confusion (shubhat al-ishtibah) and shubha of the place (shubhat al-mahall), citing Fath al-Qadir. The conclusion is that in this case, the shubha is one of confusion, not of the place, because there is no ownership at all. However, despite the hadd not being applied, lineage (nasab) is established according to some scholars, but this is disputed. The commentator notes that the author should have included the full discussion from Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A woman who is permanently prohibited to the man for marriage due to blood relation, suckling, or affinity.
شبهة (shubha): A legal ambiguity that prevents the application of the hadd punishment. In this dispute, the marriage contract with a mahram is argued to create a shubha for some, but not for others.
محل التصرف (mahall al-tasarruf): The subject or object upon which a legal disposition operates. In marriage, the mahall is the woman. The definition differs between Abu Hanifa (based on purpose) and the Sahibayn (based on ruling).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, which of the following applies to a man who knowingly marries his mahram and has intercourse?
A) He is not liable for hadd because the contract creates shubha.
B) He is liable for hadd only if she was a mahram by suckling.
C) He is liable for hadd if he knew the prohibition.
D) He is liable for both hadd and ta'zir.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the hadd of zina applies to a man who knowingly marries a mahram and has intercourse with her, based on the Sahibayn's view that no shubha exists.

Shubhat al-Mahall vs. Shubhat al-Ishtibah: The Hanafi Framework
Discussion of shubha types from Fath al-Qadir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shubhat al-mahall (ambiguity in the subject) and shubhat al-ishtibah (ambiguity due to confusion) and apply the distinction to cases of hadd, nasab, and 'idda.

Core Idea
Shubha of the place requires a plausible claim of ownership; shubha of confusion arises from misperception without any basis of ownership.

The previous lesson introduced shubha as a key concept. This lesson clarifies the two types of shubha defined by Hanafi jurists: shubhat al-mahall and shubhat al-ishtibah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings on hadd, lineage (nasab), and waiting period ('idda).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of shubha
The passage from Fath al-Qadir mentions two types: shubhat al-mahall (ambiguity in the subject) and shubhat al-ishtibah (ambiguity due to confusion).
Shubhat al-mahall is also called shubha of the place; shubhat al-ishtibah is shubha of confusion.
2
Define each type based on the criteria in the text
Shubhat al-mahall arises when there is a plausible claim of ownership (like 'You and your property belong to your father') or an existing ownership (e.g., a partner in a slave). Shubhat al-ishtibah arises when the act seems lawful but there is no basis for ownership – it is a mere mistake.
The key distinguishing factor is the presence of a legal basis for ownership.
3
Apply to the mahram marriage case
The author in Fath al-Qadir concludes that the shubha in this case is shubhat al-ishtibah because there is no ownership from any aspect. The mere fact that the contract permits intercourse legally is not an ownership-based criterion.
This means the hadd is dropped, but unlike shubhat al-mahall, nasab is not established (due to consensus) and 'idda does not apply.
4
Examine the practical effects
Both types drop the hadd, but they differ on nasab and 'idda. Shubhat al-mahall generally establishes nasab and 'idda, while shubhat al-ishtibah does not. This case is an exception: nasab is not established even under shubhat al-ishtibah because of consensus, and 'idda similarly.
The commentator notes that the rulings are not entirely consistent, showing the nuance in Hanafi fiqh.

قوله: (وبمحرم (نكحها أي لا يجب الحد بوطء امرأة محرم له عقد عليها عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : عليه الحد إذا كان عالماً بذلك لأنه عقد لم يصادف محله فيلغو كما إذا أضيف إلى الذكور. وهذا لأن محل التصرف ما يكون محلاً لحكمه وحكمه في الحل وهي من المحرمات. ولأبي حنيفة أن العقد صادف محله لأن محل التصرف ما يقبل مقصوده والأنثى من بنات آدم قابلة للتوالد وهو المقصود وكان ينبغي أن ينعقد في حق جميع الأحكام إلا أنه تقاعد عن إفادة حقيقة الحل فيورث الشبهة لأن الشبهة ما بشبه الثابت لا نفس الثابت. وحاصل الخلاف أن هذا العقد هل يوجب شبهة أم لا، ومداره أنه هل ورده على ما محله أو لا؟ هو فعند الإمام ورد على ما هو محله محليتها للعقد من حيث هو والإمام حيث أثبت محليتها أراد محليتها لنفس العقد لا بالنظر إلى خصوص عاقد ولذا علل بقبولها مقاصده ولا ينافيه قول الأصوليين أن النهي يسير في بيت المال. قوله : ( وفي فتح القدير والأوجه الخ) أقول : ذكر في الفتح بعد هذا بأسطر ما نصه : والحاصل أنه لو اعتبر شبهة اشتباه أشكل عليه ثبوت النسب، وأطلقوا أن فيها لا يثبت النسب وإن اعتبر شبهة محل اقتضى أنه لو قال علمتها حراماً علي لعلمي بكذب النساء لا يحد، ويحد قاذفه . والحق أنه شبهة اشتباه لانعدام الملك من كل وجه وكون الإخبار يطلق الجماع شرعاً ليس هو الدليل المعتبر في شبهة المحل لأن الدليل المعتبر فيه هو ما مقتضاه ثبوت الملك نحو «أنت ومالك لأبيك» والملك القائم للشريك لا ما يطلق شرعاً مجرد الفعل غير أنه يستثنى من الحكم المرتب عليه أعني عدم ثبوت النسب للإجماع فيه، وبهذه والمعتدة ظهر عدم انضباط ما مهدوه من أحكام الشبهتين اهـ. Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a man who marries a mahram (a woman prohibited for marriage due to blood relation, suckling, or affinity) incurs the hadd penalty for zina if he has intercourse with her. The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that no hadd is required if he marries a mahram. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains the positions. Therefore, the hadd is dropped due to shubha. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the contract is void ab initio because it did not encounter a proper subject (mahall) since the woman is not capable of being a wife to this man due to her prohibition. Thus, if he knows the prohibition, the hadd applies. The dispute centers on the nature of the mahall (subject of the contract): Abu Hanifa defines it as that which accepts the purpose of the contract (procreation), while the Sahibayn define it as that which accepts the ruling (permissibility). The Sahibayn's view is adopted as the fatwa (mufta bihi) according to al-Khulasa, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi also followed it. The text also discusses the difference between shubha of confusion (shubhat al-ishtibah) and shubha of the place (shubhat al-mahall), citing Fath al-Qadir. The conclusion is that in this case, the shubha is one of confusion, not of the place, because there is no ownership at all. However, despite the hadd not being applied, lineage (nasab) is established according to some scholars, but this is disputed. The commentator notes that the author should have included the full discussion from Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
شبهة المحل (shubhat al-mahall): Legal ambiguity arising from a plausible claim or basis of ownership, e.g., mistakenly believing a slave girl is one's own due to a partnership or a general statement like 'you and your property belong to your father'.
شبهة الاشتباه (shubhat al-ishtibah): Legal ambiguity due to simple confusion or misperception, without any basis of ownership. E.g., mistaking a woman for one's wife.
محل (mahall): The subject of a legal disposition; in the context of shubha, it refers to the object that one may claim ownership over.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir, the shubha in a case of marrying a mahram is classified as:
A) Shubhat al-mahall
B) Shubhat al-ishtibah
C) Shubhat al-ijma'
D) Shubhat al-ibtida'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the distinction between shubhat al-mahall and shubhat al-ishtibah is critical; the former requires a basis of ownership, while the latter arises from pure confusion.

Believing by Zann is Not Kufr
Clarifying that istihlal by zann is not kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between istihlal based on zann and istihlal based on knowing defiance, and explain the Hanafi ruling that the former does not cause kufr but may incur ta'zir.

Core Idea
Zann-based permissibility does not make one a kafir; only knowing defiance does.

This lesson draws a critical line in Islamic penal theology: the difference between a mistaken but plausible interpretation (zann) and outright rejection of a clear ruling. Using the case of marrying a mahram with honest ignorance, the Hanafi jurists established that such a person is not a kafir but is subject to ta'zir. The same principle extends to analogous situations, as clarified by al-Qurtubi on the distinction between claiming knowledge of the unseen (kufr) and mere conjecture (sinful but not kufr).

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Articulate the principle: istihlal based on zann is not kufr.
2
Find the proof
Identify the consensus case of mahram marriage where the person is not hadded and not declared kafir.
Consensus (ijma) of the fuqaha.
3
Understand the analogy
Compare with Qurtubi's discussion: claiming knowledge of the unseen is kufr; claiming conjecture is not.
Analogous reasoning (talil).
4
Apply to new scenarios
Consider a person who mistakenly believes a clear prohibition is mild or contextual. As long as it is a genuine zann, he remains a Muslim.
The act itself remains haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن مسائلهم هنا تدل على أن من استحل ما حرمه الله على وجه الظن لا يكفر وإنما يكفر إذا اعتقد الحرام حلالاً لا إذا ظنه حلالاً، ألا ترى أنهم قالوا في نكاح المحرم لو ظن الحل فإنه لا يحد بالإجماع ويعزر كما في الظهيرية وغيرها، ولم يقل أحد أنه يكفر، وكذا في نظائره وهو نظير ما ذكره القرطبي في شرح مسلم: إن ظن الغيب جائز كظن المنجم والرمال بوقوع شيء في المستقبل بتجربة أمر عادي فهو ظن صادق، والممنوع هو ادعاء علم الغيب والظاهر أن ادعاء ظن الغيب حرام وليس بكفر بخلاف ادعاء علم الغيب فإنه كفر وسنوضحه إن شاء الله تعالى في باب الردة. وأشار المصنف إلى أن المستأجرة للزنا لو وطئها فلا حد عليه لشبهة العقد عند الإمام لأن المستوفى بالزنا المنفعة المعقود عليه في الإجارة وقالا يحد كما سيأتي. وأطلق في المحرم فشمل المحرم نسباً ورضاعاً وصهرية، وأشار إلى أنه لو عقد على منكوحة الغير أو معتدته أو مطلقته الثلاث أو أمة على حرة أو تزوج مجوسية أو أمة بلا إذن سيدها أو تزوج العبد بلا إذن سيده أو تزوج خمساً في عقدة فوطئهن أو جمع بين أختين في عقدة فوطئهما أو الأخيرة لو كان متعاقباً بعد التزوج فإنه لا حد بالوطء بالأولى وهو بالاتفاق على الأظهر أما عنده فظاهر، وأما عندهما ألا.
Then know that their rulings here indicate that whoever deems as permissible what Allah has forbidden out of conjecture (zann) does not become an unbeliever; he only becomes an unbeliever if he believes the forbidden to be permissible, not if he supposes it to be permissible. Do you not see that they said regarding marriage to a mahram: if he assumed permissibility, he is not hadded by consensus, and he is given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) as in al-Zahiriyya and others, and no one said he becomes an unbeliever. Likewise in its analogues. It is analogous to what al-Qurtubi mentioned in his commentary on Sahih Muslim: that conjecture about the unseen is permissible, like the conjecture of an astrologer or a diviner about something occurring in the future based on ordinary experience, for it is a true conjecture. What is prohibited is the claim of knowledge of the unseen. It appears that claiming conjecture about the unseen is forbidden but not kufr, unlike claiming knowledge of the unseen, which is kufr, and we will explain it, Allah willing, in the chapter on apostasy. And the author indicated that if a hired woman for zina is intercourse with, then no hadd is upon him due to the shubha of the contract according to the Imam, because what is received through zina is the benefit that was contracted upon in the hiring (ijara). The two said: he is to be hadded, as will come. And he spoke absolutely regarding the mahram, so it includes mahram by lineage, suckling, and affinity. And he indicated that if he contracts marriage with a married woman, or a woman in her waiting period ('idda), or his wife thrice divorced, or a slave-girl while having a free wife, or marries a Zoroastrian woman, or a slave-girl without her master's permission, or a slave marries without his master's permission, or marries five women in one contract and has intercourse with all of them, or joins two sisters in one contract and has intercourse with both of them, or the last one if they were successive after marriage, then there is no hadd for intercourse with the first, and this is by agreement on the most apparent. As for according to him (Abu Hanifa), it is clear; as for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), [it is different].
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage establishes a key principle: when a person mistakenly believes something forbidden to be permissible based on a plausible interpretation (zann), this does not constitute kufr (disbelief). Kufr only occurs if one believes that the forbidden is permissible despite knowing the clear prohibition. The proof is subtle: the jurists ruled that even in cases of clear prohibition (like marrying a mahram), if someone honestly believed it was permissible, he is not subject to hadd by consensus, but only to ta'zir (discretionary punishment), and no one declares him a kafir. This principle is applied across many cases. The commentator then lists multiple scenarios from the author's text where the hadd for zina is not applied due to shubha (legal ambiguity). These include: (1) a woman hired for zina (musta'jara) — according to Abu Hanifa, because the benefit received is the same as contracted in the hire agreement, creating a shubha; (2) marriage to a mahram (by nasab, rada', or musahara); (3) marriage to a married woman, a woman in 'idda, or a thrice-divorced woman; (4) marriage to a slave-girl while already married to a free woman, or to a Zoroastrian, or to a slave-girl without permission; (5) a slave marrying without permission; (6) marrying five women in one contract; (7) marrying two sisters in one contract. For the first such marriage in these cases, the hadd is not applied according to the most apparent view. The commentator notes that Abu Hanifa's position is clear, while the Sahibayn may differ in some cases, particularly the hired prostitute. The overarching theme is that shubha from various sources has a significant impact on penal law (hudud), even though the underlying acts are sinful.

Key Terms
ظن (zann): A strong but uncertain belief; here, it refers to a mistaken belief that something haram is permissible based on plausible reasoning.
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood, suckling, or affinity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what happens to a person who marries a mahram assuming it is permissible?
A) He is executed for zina and apostasy.
B) He is not subject to hadd but is given ta'zir, and is not declared a kafir.
C) He is excused entirely and the marriage is valid.
D) He is considered a kafir because he violated a clear prohibition.

Key Takeaway
The line between sin and disbelief is drawn by knowledge and defiance, not by mere violation of a ruling while ignorant.

Cases Where Hadd for Zina is Dropped Due to Shubha
Listing cases where hadd is not applied due to shubha in marriage contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the specific cases where the hadd of zina is not applied due to shubha, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the hired prostitute.

Core Idea
Hadd is dropped when a shubha (legal ambiguity) exists, even if the act is sinful.

This lesson surveys numerous marriage-like scenarios where, despite the presence of intercourse outside a valid marriage, the fixed punishment (hadd) of zina is not applied. The Hanafi school identifies a shubha in the contract or status that undermines the certainty of the prohibition. The author lists cases involving mahram, married women, divorced women, slave-girls, and multiple marriages, and highlights a notable internal dispute: the hired prostitute (musta'jara) case, where Imam Abu Hanifa sees a shubha while the Sahibayn do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cases
List all cases from the text: mahram, married woman, woman in 'idda, thrice-divorced woman, slave-girl with a free wife, Zoroastrian woman, slave-girl without permission, slave without permission, five in one contract, two sisters in one contract.
Also includes the hired prostitute (musta'jara).
2
Understand the shubha
In each case, there is a semblance of validity in the contract or a plausible mistake that creates doubt.
For example, marrying a mahram: the person might not know the prohibition.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Focus on the musta'jara case: Abu Hanifa analogizes to ijara (hire) and drops the hadd; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad impose hadd.
This is a genuine ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Synthesize the principle
The common thread is that any shubha in the contract or in the person's understanding that creates doubt about the unlawfulness of the act leads to dropping the hadd.
Hadd is only for clear, unambiguous zina.

Source Text

ثم اعلم أن مسائلهم هنا تدل على أن من استحل ما حرمه الله على وجه الظن لا يكفر وإنما يكفر إذا اعتقد الحرام حلالاً لا إذا ظنه حلالاً، ألا ترى أنهم قالوا في نكاح المحرم لو ظن الحل فإنه لا يحد بالإجماع ويعزر كما في الظهيرية وغيرها، ولم يقل أحد أنه يكفر، وكذا في نظائره وهو نظير ما ذكره القرطبي في شرح مسلم: إن ظن الغيب جائز كظن المنجم والرمال بوقوع شيء في المستقبل بتجربة أمر عادي فهو ظن صادق، والممنوع هو ادعاء علم الغيب والظاهر أن ادعاء ظن الغيب حرام وليس بكفر بخلاف ادعاء علم الغيب فإنه كفر وسنوضحه إن شاء الله تعالى في باب الردة. وأشار المصنف إلى أن المستأجرة للزنا لو وطئها فلا حد عليه لشبهة العقد عند الإمام لأن المستوفى بالزنا المنفعة المعقود عليه في الإجارة وقالا يحد كما سيأتي. وأطلق في المحرم فشمل المحرم نسباً ورضاعاً وصهرية، وأشار إلى أنه لو عقد على منكوحة الغير أو معتدته أو مطلقته الثلاث أو أمة على حرة أو تزوج مجوسية أو أمة بلا إذن سيدها أو تزوج العبد بلا إذن سيده أو تزوج خمساً في عقدة فوطئهن أو جمع بين أختين في عقدة فوطئهما أو الأخيرة لو كان متعاقباً بعد التزوج فإنه لا حد بالوطء بالأولى وهو بالاتفاق على الأظهر أما عنده فظاهر، وأما عندهما ألا.
Then know that their rulings here indicate that whoever deems as permissible what Allah has forbidden out of conjecture (zann) does not become an unbeliever; he only becomes an unbeliever if he believes the forbidden to be permissible, not if he supposes it to be permissible. Do you not see that they said regarding marriage to a mahram: if he assumed permissibility, he is not hadded by consensus, and he is given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) as in al-Zahiriyya and others, and no one said he becomes an unbeliever. Likewise in its analogues. It is analogous to what al-Qurtubi mentioned in his commentary on Sahih Muslim: that conjecture about the unseen is permissible, like the conjecture of an astrologer or a diviner about something occurring in the future based on ordinary experience, for it is a true conjecture. What is prohibited is the claim of knowledge of the unseen. Anal Intercourse and Liwat: Hadd vs. Ta'zir – An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadd for anal intercourse and liwat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether anal intercourse and liwat are subject to hadd, and explain the qiyas and counterarguments involved.

Core Idea
Anal intercourse is not zina according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn analogize it to zina, creating a key hadd/ta'zir dispute.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: does anal intercourse (with a woman or boy) entail the hadd punishment for zina? Abu Hanifa distinguishes it from zina, while the Sahibayn apply qiyas to extend the hadd. Understanding the arguments and their practical consequences is essential for grasping the nuances of Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts and the Dispute
Read the passage to identify which two specific acts are under discussion (anal intercourse with a foreign woman, and liwat with a boy) and the two opposing positions: Abu Hanifa says no hadd, the Sahibayn say it carries hadd like zina.
2
Follow the Sahibayn's Qiyas
Deconstruct the qiyas: the asl is vaginal zina, the far' is anal intercourse, and the illa is 'fulfillment of desire in a desired place with intent to discharge.' Note how the Sahibayn argue that the act is purely unlawful and complete.
The illa is extracted by tahqiq al-manat.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's Response
Identify Abu Hanifa's two main objections: (1) the Companions disagreed on the punishment, indicating it is not a fixed hadd, and (2) there is no lineage confusion, making the act rarer and not analogous to zina in that respect.
He also interprets the hadith about killing as siyasa or for one who considers it lawful.
4
Recognize the Siyasa Option
The passage mentions that the imam (ruler) may impose severe punishment, including death, as a matter of policy for habitual offenders, but this is not the qadi's domain.
Siyasa is a discretionary tool, not a fixed hadd.
5
Clarify the Scope of the Sahibayn's Disagreement
Note that the Sahibayn only impose hadd for mahram relatives, not for every prohibited woman (e.g., a fifth wife or a woman in iddah). This narrows the dispute from what might appear to be a blanket rule.
The text clarifies this through references to al-Kafi and Ibn al-Mundhir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي أجنبية في غير قبل ولواطة أي لا يجب الحد في مسألتين أيضاً: الأولى لو وطئ امرأة أجنبية في دبرها فإنه لا يحد الثانية لو لاط بصبي في دبره فإنه لا يحد. ولا شك أن وطء الأجنبية في دبرها لواطة أيضاً، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : هو كالزنا فيحد رجماً إن كان محصناً أو جلداً إن كان غير محصن لأنه في معنى الزنا لأنه قضاء الشهوة في محل مشتهى على سبيل الكمال على وجه تمحض حراماً لقصد سفح الماء. وله أنه ليس بزنا الله لاختلاف الصحابة رضي عنهم في موجبه من الإحراق بالنار وهدم الجدار والتنكيس من مكان مرتفع باتباع الأحجار ونحو ذلك، ولا هو في معنى الزنا لأنه ليس فيه إضاعة الولد و اشتباه الأنساب ولذا هو أندر وقوعاً لانعدام الداعي في أحد الوجهين والداعي إلى الزنا من الجانبين، وما ورد في الحديث من الأمر بقتل الفاعل والمفعول به فمحمول على السياسة أو على المستحل . قال الزيلعي : لو رأى الإمام مصلحة في قتل من اعتاده جاز له قتله ا هـ . واعلم أنهم يذكرون في حكم السياسة أن الإمام يفعلها ولم يقولوا القاضي فظاهره أن القاضي ليس له الحكم بالسياسة ولا العمل بها قيد بعدم الحد لأن التعزير واجب. قالوا: يوجع المحقق في الفتح حيث قال : ثم قول حافظ الدين في الكافي في تعليل سقوط الحد في تزوج المجوسية وما معها لأن الشبهة إنما تنتفي عندهما يعني حتى يجب الحد إذا كان مجمعاً على تحريمه وهي حرام على التأبيد يقتضي أن لا يجد عندهما في تزوج منكوحة الغير وما معها لأنها ليست محرمة على التأبيد فإن حرمتها مقيدة ببقاء نكاحها وعدتها كما أن حرمة المجوسية مغياة بتمجسها حتى لو أسلمت حلت كما أن تلك لو طلقت وانقضت عدتها حلت وأنه لا يحد عندهما إلا في المحارم فقط، وهذا هو الذي يغلب على ظني والذين يعتمد على نقلهم وتحريرهم مثل ابن المنذر كذلك ذكروا فحكى ابن المنذر عنهما أنه يحد في ذات المحرم ولا يحد في غير ذلك قال : مثل أن يتزوج مجوسية أو خامسة أو معتدة وعبارة الكافي للحاكم تفيد ذلك حيث قال: رجل تزوج لا يحل له نكاحها فدخل بها قال : لا حد عليه وإن فعله على علم لم يحد أيضاً عقوبة في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : إن علم بذلك فعليه الحد في ذوات المحارم. إلى هنا لفظه فعمم في المرأة التي لا تحل له في سقوط الحد على قول أبي حنيفة، ثم خص مخالفتهما بذوات المحارم من ذلك العموم فاللفظ ظاهر في ذلك على ما عرف في الروايات اهـ. ومراده بذلك الرد على ما نقله حافظ الدين في الكافي حيث قال : منكوحة الغير ومعتدته ومطلقة الثلاث بعد التزويج كالمحرم وإن كان النكاح مختلفاً فيه كالنكاح بلا ولي ولا شهود فلا حد عليه اتفاقاً. وفي النهر : هنا سقط أو إيجاز مخل فليتنبه له قوله : (فمحمول على السياسة) تقدم تفسيرها امرأة ممن ويوجع
His saying: 'And regarding a foreign woman in other than the front, and liwat' i.e., the hadd is not obligatory in two additional issues: First, if one has anal intercourse with a foreign woman, then he is not punished with hadd. Second, if one commits liwat (sodomy) with a boy in his anus, then he is not punished with hadd. There is no doubt that anal intercourse with a foreign woman is also liwat, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is like zina, so he is punished with stoning if he is muhsan or lashes if he is not muhsan, because it is in the meaning of zina: it is the fulfillment of desire in a desired place in a complete manner, purely unlawful with the intent of discharging water. And his (Abu Hanifa's) evidence is that it is not zina because the Companions differed on its punishment: some said burning with fire, destroying the wall, throwing from a height followed by stones, etc. Nor is it in the meaning of zina because it does not involve wasting lineage and confusing lineage, and therefore it is rarer due to lack of motive on one side, while the motive for zina is from both sides. And what is reported in the hadith about killing the doer and the one with whom it is done is interpreted as a discretionary punishment (siyasa) or as applying to one who considers it lawful. Al-Zayla'i said: If the imam sees a benefit in killing someone who habitually practices it, it is permissible for him to kill him. And know that they mention in the ruling of siyasa that the imam does it and they did not say the qadi, so the apparent is that the qadi does not have the authority of siyasa nor acting by it. The condition is that there is no hadd because ta'zir is obligatory. They said: he is beaten... The muhaqqiq said in al-Fath: Then the statement of Hafiz al-Din in al-Kafi in his explanation of the dropping of hadd in marrying a Zoroastrian woman and what is with it: because shubha is only negated according to them (the Sahibayn) meaning that hadd is obligatory when it is unanimously prohibited and it is permanently prohibited. This implies that they do not impose hadd in marrying another's wife and what is with it because it is not permanently prohibited; indeed its prohibition is tied to the continuance of her marriage and waiting period, just as the prohibition of a Zoroastrian woman is tied to her Zoroastrianism until she becomes Muslim, she becomes permissible, and just as that woman if she divorces and finishes her waiting period, she becomes permissible. And that they only impose hadd for mahram relatives. And this is what dominates my opinion, and those who rely on their transmission and editing like Ibn al-Mundhir mentioned similarly. So Ibn al-Mundhir narrated from them that they impose hadd for a mahram woman and do not impose hadd for other than that. He said: such as marrying a Zoroastrian woman, or a fifth wife, or a woman in waiting period. And the wording of al-Kafi by al-Hakim indicates that: a man marries a woman who is not permissible for him to marry, then he enters upon her, he said: there is no hadd upon him even if he does it knowingly, he is not punished as a penalty according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: if he knows that, then upon him is hadd for mahram women. Up to here his wording. So he generalizes that for women who are not permissible for him, the hadd is dropped according to Abu Hanifa, then he specifies their disagreement to mahram women from that generality. So the wording is apparent in that according to what is known in the narrations. And his intent by that is to respond to what Hafiz al-Din transmitted in al-Kafi where he said: another's wife, her waiting-period woman, and the thrice-divorced woman after marriage are like the mahram, and if the marriage is disputed like marriage without a guardian and witnesses, then there is no hadd by agreement. And in al-Nahr: here there is an omission or defective abridgment, so one should pay attention. His saying: (it is interpreted as siyasa) its explanation has preceded. A woman from... and he is beaten.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding anal intercourse (with a woman or boy) and liwat. Abu Hanifa holds that these acts are not zina and therefore do not require hadd; instead, the perpetrator receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment). His evidence includes the disagreement among the Companions about the appropriate punishment, and the fact that these acts do not lead to lineage confusion (as zina does). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize these acts to zina because they involve the fulfillment of sexual desire in a desirable place with intent to ejaculate. They argue that the hadd of zina should apply. The text also discusses the concept of siyasa (discretionary punishment by the ruler), noting that the imam may impose severe punishment (even death) for habitual offenders as a matter of policy, but this is not the qadi's domain. The latter part of the passage returns to the scope of the disagreement in the previous lesson, clarifying that the Sahibayn only impose hadd for mahram relatives, not for other temporary prohibitions. This underscores that the disagreement is narrower than might be thought.

Key Terms
وطء الأجنبية في الدبر (wat' al-ajnabiyya fi al-dubr): Anal intercourse with a foreign woman. In this text, it is classified as liwat.
لواط (liwat): Sodomy, specifically anal intercourse with a male. In Hanafi fiqh, it is distinct from zina.
سياسة (siyasa): Discretionary punishment by the ruler (imam) for public interest, not a fixed hadd or ta'zir by the qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling on a man who commits liwat with a boy?
A) He receives hadd (stoning if muhsan, lashes if not).
B) He receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
C) He is killed by the qadi under siyasa.
D) He receives no punishment because the act is not prohibited.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is divided: anal intercourse is not zina for Abu Hanifa (ta'zir only), but the Sahibayn apply hadd via qiyas.

Liwatah and Bestiality: Acts Not Subject to Hadd – The Hanafi Position
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether liwatah and bestiality incur hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liwatah and bestiality, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the reasoning behind the non-application of hadd.

Core Idea
Liwatah does not incur hadd because it lacks elements of wasting seed and confusing lineage, which are the bases for zina's severity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether liwatah (anal intercourse) and bestiality incur the fixed punishment (hadd) of zina. Abu Hanifa holds that they do not, while the Sahibayn treat them as zina. The passage provides the proof structure, highlighting how the Companions' disagreement and the distinct nature of liwatah justify ta'zir rather than hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases where hadd is negated
First: a man who has intercourse with a foreign woman in her anus. Second: a man who commits liwatah with a boy. Both are liwatah and do not incur hadd according to Abu Hanifa.
The text explicitly mentions both cases as separate but equivalent.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and the Sahibayn's opposing ruling
Abu Hanifa: no hadd, only ta'zir. Sahibayn: hadd applies (stoning if muhsan, flogging if not). The thamarah al-khilaf is the difference in punishment.
This is the core ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
The Companions disagreed on punishment (burning, wall demolition, throwing from height). The act does not cause confusion of lineage, unlike zina. The hadith commanding killing is interpreted as siyasah or for those who consider it permissible.
The absence of lineage confusion is key: zina's hadd is meant to preserve lineage.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's dalil
They compare liwatah to zina via qiyas: both involve fulfilling lust in a desired place, completely forbidden, with intent to ejaculate.
The argument uses qiyas khafi (hidden analogy), which Abu Hanifa rejects due to the fundamental difference.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical application
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: no hadd. The qadi applies ta'zir (discretionary punishment) and may imprison or beat severely. The imam may use siyasah to kill habitual offenders.
Ta'zir is determined by the judge's discretion based on the severity and the perpetrator's state.

Chapter of Hudud: Chapter on Intercourse that Obligates Hadd and That Which Does Not. Because the legal doubt (shubhah) is only negated according to them (Sahibayn) when the act is unanimously prohibited and it is perpetually forbidden. And he restricted [the negation of hadd] because ta'zir is obligatory if [the perpetrator] is knowledgeable. They said: he should be beaten severely with the most severe ta'zir as a policy. His statement: 'And with a foreign woman in other than the vagina, and liwatah' i.e., hadd is not obligatory in two matters as well: first, if he has intercourse with a foreign woman in her anus, then he is not subjected to hadd; second, if he commits liwatah with a boy in his anus, then he is not subjected to hadd. There is no doubt that intercourse with a foreign woman in her anus is also liwatah, and this is according to Abu Hanifah. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is like zina, so he is stoned if he is muhsan, or flogged if he is non-muhsan, because it is in the meaning of zina: fulfilling lust in a desired place in a complete manner, purely forbidden, with the intent of ejaculation. And for him (Abu Hanifah) [the argument] is that it is not zina because of the disagreement of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) regarding its punishment: burning with fire, demolishing a wall, throwing from a high place while following with stones, and so on. Nor is it in the meaning of zina because it does not involve loss of lineage and confusion of parentage, hence it occurs more rarely due to lack of motive in one of the two ways, whereas the motive for zina is from both sides. And the hadith commanding the killing of the active and passive participant is interpreted as a policy (siyasah) or applied to the one who considers it permissible. Al-Zayla'i said: if the imam sees a benefit in killing one who habitually practices it, he may kill him. And know that they mention in the ruling of siyasah that the imam does it, and they did not say the qadi, so apparently the qadi has no authority to judge by siyasah or to act upon it. He restricted it by the negation of hadd because ta'zir is obligatory. They said: he is beaten... (then the text continues with detailed commentary including a lengthy discussion on the scope of the dispute, other rulings for liwatah, and then the ruling on bestiality). (Then the text relates a discussion about whether liwatah will be in Paradise, including an exchange between Ibn al-Walid and Abu Yusuf al-Qazwini, and concludes with the point about the animal.)
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the topic of sexual acts that do not incur hadd punishment. The author begins by stating two cases: (1) vaginal intercourse with a foreign woman in her anus, and (2) liwatah with a boy. According to Abu Hanifa, neither act incurs hadd. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, equating these acts with zina and applying the same hadd (stoning or flogging). The text then provides Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the Companions differed on the punishment (some prescribed burning, etc.), and unlike zina, liwatah does not cause confusion of lineage. Therefore, it is rarer and lacks the same motive. The hadith commanding execution is explained as a matter of siyasah (policy) or applies only to one who considers liwatah permissible. The author clarifies that ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is still obligatory for those who are aware of the prohibition. The discussion then expands to a related issue about marriage to a Magian woman, referencing different opinions on when shubhah negates hadd. The passage also lists various legal consequences unique to liwatah: no mahr (dower), no 'iddah, no prohibition of remarriage to a former spouse, no retaliation for false accusation (qadhf), no li'an, etc. Finally, the text covers bestiality, stating that it also incurs no hadd because it is not analogous to zina; it is repulsive to sound nature and arises only from extreme folly or excessive lust. The animal is to be slaughtered (if edible) or killed, but this is not obligatory. The passage ends with a theological discussion on whether liwatah could exist in Paradise, concluding it will not, based on Quranic verses condemning it.

Key Terms
لواطة (liwāṭah): Anal intercourse, either with a male or a female (in the anus). The text treats vaginal intercourse in the anus as liwatah.
سياسة (siyāsah): Discretionary policy or punishment carried out by the imam or ruler for public interest, not a fixed hadd.
تعزير (taʿzīr): A discretionary punitive measure (beating, imprisonment, etc.) applied for acts that are sinful but do not have a fixed hadd punishment.
حد (ḥadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah (e.g., stoning, flogging) for specific crimes like zina, theft, etc.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt or uncertainty that negates the application of hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is punished with stoning if the perpetrator is muhsan.
B) It incurs ta'zir but not hadd.
C) It is treated exactly like zina in all aspects.
D) It is permissible if done in marriage.

Key Takeaway
Liwatah and bestiality are haram but do not incur hadd; they are punished by ta'zir according to the Hanafi school.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Punishment for habitual sodomy and its severity
Ruling on the punishment and legal consequences of sodomy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the punishment for habitual sodomy (liwat), explain why no hadd is prescribed, and identify the unique subsidiary rulings that distinguish it from zina.

Core Idea
Sodomy is more severely prohibited than zina, yet no hadd applies due to lack of textual evidence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a challenging aspect of Hanafi hudud: why sodomy, despite being considered more severe than zina, does not incur the fixed hadd punishment. It clarifies that the absence of hadd is not a sign of leniency but rather a consequence of the lack of a specific dalil. Additionally, the text enumerates several unique legal consequences of sodomy, distinguishing it from zina. Our focus will be on understanding the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and the practical implications for a judge or jurist.

Guided Path
1
State the main ruling
Identify the Hanafi position on the punishment for habitual sodomy. The text states that the Imam may kill him as a discretionary policy (siyasah), not as a fixed hadd. For non-habitual, ta'zir (flogging, imprisonment) is prescribed.
Contrast with zina which has a fixed hadd.
2
Understand why no hadd is prescribed
Abu Hanifa did not prescribe hadd for sodomy because there is no clear evidence (dalil) from Quran or Sunnah establishing a fixed punishment. This is not because the act is less sinful; rather, it is more sinful, but the absence of a specific hadd means the ruler uses discretion.
The text emphasizes that hadd is purifying, so its absence makes the punishment more severe in a sense.
3
Examine the nature of sodomy's prohibition
The text, citing al-Akmal, states that sodomy is forbidden by intellect ('aql), law (shar'), and nature (tab'), whereas zina is forbidden only by law and not by nature. Thus, sodomy is inherently more repugnant.
This explains the perceived severity.
4
List the subsidiary legal rulings
The passage mentions several consequences unique to sodomy: no marriage gift ('uqr), no 'iddah in a defective marriage or doubtful intercourse, no return to first husband, no revocability, no prohibition of marriage by affinity, no expiation in Ramadan, no hadd for false accusation (qadhf), and no li'an. Also, ghusl is obligatory on both parties.
These differentiate sodomy from zina.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi differences
The text notes that regarding qadhf (false accusation) of sodomy and li'an, Abu Hanifa holds that no hadd and no li'an apply, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. This shows internal differences within the Hanafi school.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) follows Abu Hanifa on the absence of hadd for sodomy itself, but on subsidiary issues there is variation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضرباً زاد في الجامع الصغير أنه يودع في السجن. قال في فتح القدير: حتى يموت أو يتوب، ولو اعتاد اللواطة قتله الإمام محصناً كان أو غير محصن سياسة. وذكر العلامة الأكمل في شرح المشارق أن اللواطة محرمة عقلاً وشرعاً وطبعاً بخلاف الزنا فإنه ليس بحرام طبعاً فكانت أشد حرمة منه وإنما لم يوجب الحد أبو حنيفة فيها لعدم الدليل عليه لا لخفتها. وإنما عدم الوجوب فيها للتغليظ على الفاعل لأن الحد مطهر على قول بعض العلماء. وقيد بالأجنبية ليفيد أن زوجته وجاريته بالأولى في عدم وجوب الحد لكن قال في التبيين : إذا فعل في عبده أو أمته أو منكوحته لا يجب الحد بالإجماع وإنما يعزر لارتكابه المحظور. وفي الحاوي القدسي : وتكلموا في هذا التعزير من الجلد ورميه من أعلى موضع وحبسه في أنتن بقعة سوى الإخصاء والجب والجلد أصح .اهـ. وللواطة أحكام أخر لا يجب بها العقر أي المهر ولا العدة في النكاح الفاسد ولا في المأتي بها لشبهة ولا تحل للزوج الأول في النكاح الصحيح، ولا تثبت بها الرجعة ولا حرمة المصاهرة عند الأكثر، ولا الكفارة في رمضان في رواية ولو قذف بها لا يحد خلافاً لهما، وكذا لو قذف امرأته بها لم يلاعن خلافاً لهما، وعن الصفار يكفر مستحلها عند الجمهور ؛ كذا في المجتبى : وقدمنا أنه يجب الغسل بها على الفاعل والمفعول به
Striking. He added in al-Jami' al-Saghir that he is imprisoned in prison. He said in Fath al-Qadir: until he dies or repents. And if he is accustomed to sodomy, the Imam kills him, whether he is muhsan or not, as a policy. The illustrious al-Akmal mentioned in Sharh al-Mashariq that sodomy is forbidden by intellect, law, and nature, unlike zina which is not forbidden by nature, so it is more severe in prohibition than it. And Abu Hanifa did not prescribe hadd for it due to the absence of evidence for it, not because of its lightness. Rather, the absence of obligation in it is to make it severe for the doer because hadd is purifying according to some scholars. And he restricted it to [a non-mahram] woman to indicate that his wife and his slave-woman are more deserving of not having the hadd, but he said in al-Tabyin: If he does it with his slave, his slave-woman, or his married woman, hadd is not obligatory by consensus, and he is only disciplined (ta'zir) for committing the prohibited act. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: They discussed this ta'zir: flogging, throwing him from a high place, imprisoning him in the foulest spot, except castration and gelding; flogging is most sound. End. And sodomy has other rulings: ‘uqr (i.e., mahr) is not obligatory due to it, nor ‘iddah in a defective marriage, nor in the one penetrated due to a doubt; she does not become permissible for the first husband in a valid marriage; no revocability (ruj‘ah) is established by it, nor prohibition of marriage by affinity according to most; no expiation in Ramadan in one narration; if he accuses of it, he is not flogged (hadd), contrary to the two [companions]; likewise, if he accuses his wife of it, he does not engage in li‘an, contrary to the two; and from al-Saffar: the one who deems it lawful becomes an unbeliever according to the majority; as in al-Mujtaba: And we have preceded that ghusl is obligatory due to it on the active and passive participant.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage, from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the chapter on hudud, specifically the section on intercourse that necessitates hadd and that which does not. It begins by addressing the punishment for habitual sodomy (liwat). The author clarifies that the Imam may execute a habitual sodomite as a matter of discretionary policy (siyasah), regardless of ihsan (being married). Then it discusses the nature of sodomy: it is forbidden by intellect, revelation, and natural disposition, whereas zina (fornication) is only forbidden by revelation, not by nature. Hence sodomy is considered more severe in prohibition. However, Imam Abu Hanifa did not prescribe the fixed hadd punishment for sodomy because there is no clear textual evidence (dalil) for it—not because it is less serious. Rather, the absence of hadd is itself a form of severity, since hadd would purify the offender (according to some scholars). The passage then lists special rulings for sodomy: no mahr, no iddah, the person does not become halal for the first husband, no ruj'ah, no prohibition of marriage by affinity, no expiation in Ramadan (in one narration), and no hadd for slander of sodomy (unlike slander of zina). Also, if a man accuses his wife of sodomy, li'an is not performed (according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Finally, it states that ghusl is obligatory for both the active and passive participant.

Key Terms
اللواطة (al-liwāṭah): Sodomy, specifically sexual intercourse with a male (anal intercourse).
سياسة (siyāsah): Discretionary punishment by the ruler in the public interest, not fixed by shari'ah.
التعزير (al-ta‘zīr): Discretionary punishment less than hadd, used for crimes without fixed punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because there is no clear evidence (dalil) for it

D) Because Abu Hanifa considered it a minor offense

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sodomy is more severely prohibited than zina yet carries no fixed hadd; its punishment is discretionary ta'zir or execution under siyasah, and it has unique legal consequences that distinguish it from zina.
