Zina with a Female Slave and Killing Her: Hadd and Value Due
Ruling with proof: zina with amah and killing her

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person commits zina with a female slave and kills her, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Both hadd and value are due for zina and killing an amah; liability for killing does not create retroactive ownership.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific scenario where a man commits zina with a female slave (amah) and kills her during the act. The ruling combines criminal and financial penalties. The author provides the main position and an intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf, along with the response from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? Zina with an amah followed by killing her. What is the ruling? Both hadd and value are due. Note the exception for the caliph: retaliation and financial penalties, not hadd.
2
Locate the dalil for hadd
The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nur:2) with the imperative 'fajlidu' indicates obligation (wujub) of flogging for zina.
The dalil is qat'i in thubut and dalala.
3
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf argues that payment of value creates ownership, so the hadd drops – analogous to purchasing the slave after zina. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the guarantee is for killing, not for the usufruct, so no retroactive ownership arises.
Key distinction: killing destroys the entity, while destroying a limb leaves the entity intact, which does create doubt (shubhah).
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The guarantee for killing does not create ownership in the consumed usufruct. Ownership would be retroactive but cannot affect what is already consumed (the sexual act). This is unlike the case of destroying an eye where the physical body remains and ownership creates shubhah.
The analogy to stolen property (ownership before amputation drops hadd) is rejected because the slave's usufruct was consumed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: both hadd and value are due. This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in fatwa, both penalties are imposed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود باب الوطء الذي يوجب الحد والذي لا يوجبه زنى بأمة فقتلها لزمه الحد والقيمة والخليفة يؤخذ بالقصاص والأموال لا بالحد . وإن كان دم ولو كان والقيمة معناه قتلها بفعل الزنا لأنه جنى جنايتين فيوفر على كل واحدة منهما حكمها. وعن أبي يوسف أنه لا يحد لأن تقرر ضمان القيمة سبب لملك الأمة وصار كما إذا اشتراها بعد ما زنى بها وهو على هذا الخلاف واعتراض سبب الملك قبل إقامة الحد يوجب سقوطه كما إذا ملك المسروق قبل القطع ولهما أنه ضمان قتل فلا . الملك لأن ضمان يوجب يوجبه إنما يوجبه في العين كما في هبة المسروق لا في منافع البضع لأنها استوفيت والملك يثبت مستنداً فلا يظهر في المستوفى لكونها معدومة، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا زنى بها فاذهب عينها حيث يجب عليه قيمتها ويسقط الحد لأن الملك هناك يثبت في الجثة العمياء وهي عين فأورث شبهة. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو زنى بحرة فقتلها به يجب الحد عليه اتفاقاً لأن الحرة لا تملك بالضمان وإن لم يقتلها وإنما أفضاها بأن اختلط المسلكان فإن كانت كبيرة مطاوعة له من غير دعوى شبهة فعليهما الحد ولا شيء عليه في الإفضاء لرضاها به ولا مهر عليه لوجوب الحد، مع دعوى شبهة فلا حد ولا شيء في الإفضاء ويجب العقر، وإن كانت مكرهة من غير دعوى شبهة فعليه الحد دونها ولا مهر لها ثم ينظر في الإفضاء؛ فإن لم يستمسك بولها فعليه دية المرأة كاملة لأنه فوت جنس المنفعة على الكمال وإن كان يستمسك بولها حد وضمن ثلث الدية لما أن جنايته جائفة. وإن كان مع دعوى شبهة فلا حد عليهما. وإن كان البول يستمسك فعليه ثلث الدية ويجب المهر في ظاهر الرواية، وإن لم يستمسك فعليه الدية كاملة ولا يجب المهر عندهما خلافاً لمحمد وإن كانت صغيرة يجامع مثلها فهي كالكبيرة فيما ذكرنا إلا في حق سقوط الأرش برضاها، وإن كانت صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها، فإن كان يستمسك بولها لزمه ثلث الدية والمهر كاملاً ولا حد عليه لتمكن القصور في معنى الزنا وهو الإيلاج في قبل المشتهاة، ولهذا لا تثبت به حرمة المصاهرة والوطء الحرام في دار الإسلام يوجب المهر إذا انتفى الحد فيجب ثلث الدية لكونه جائفة على ما بينا، وإن كان لا يستمسك ضمن الدية ولا يضمن المهر عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد: يضمن المهر أيضاً لما ذكرنا ولنا أن الدية ضمان كل العضو والمهر ضمان جزء منه وضمان الجزء يدخل في ضمان الكل إذا كانا في عضو واحد كما إذا قطع أصبع إنسان ثم قطع كفته قبل البرء يدخل أرش الأصبع في أرش الكف ويسقط إحصانه بهذا الوطء لوجود صورة الزنا وهو الوطء الحرام. وفي المحيط : لو كسر فخذ امرأة في الزنا أو جرحها ضمن الدية في ماله وحده لأنه شبه العمد وفي شبهة تجب الدية في ماله يعني به فيما دون النفس، وإن جنت الأمة فزني بها قال الله تعالى الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا [النور: ۲] فالمعنى الذي يفيد أن فعل الزنا مع قوله أزني بك لا يجلد معه للفظ المهر معارض له اهـ. وأقره في النهر .
The Book of Hudud: Chapter on Intercourse that Incurs the Hadd and That Which Does Not. He committed zina with a female slave and killed her; both the hadd and the value are incumbent upon him. The caliph is subject to retaliation and financial penalties, not hadd. The meaning of value is that he killed her by the act of zina because he committed two crimes, so the ruling for each is applied in full. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he is not subject to hadd because the establishment of liability for the value is a cause for ownership of the slave, and it becomes as if he purchased her after having committed zina with her. This is based on the dispute and the objection that a cause of ownership before the establishment of hadd necessitates its dropping, as when one owns stolen property before amputation. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is a guarantee for killing, not ownership, because the guarantee that necessitates ownership only necessitates it in the commodity, as in a gift of stolen property, not in the usufruct of sexual intercourse because it has been enjoyed, and ownership is established retroactively, so it does not appear in what has been consumed because it is non-existent. This is unlike the case where he committed zina with her and then destroyed her eye, where he must pay her value and the hadd is dropped, because ownership there is established in the physical body, which is a commodity, so it creates doubt. The author indicated that if he committed zina with a free woman and killed her as a result, the hadd is incumbent on him by agreement, because a free woman is not owned by the guarantee. If he did not kill her but rather caused ifda' (perforation of the urinary and reproductive tracts), then if she was an adult, willing, and without a claim of doubt, both receive the hadd, and nothing is required from him for the ifda' due to her consent, and no dower is due because of the hadd. If there is a claim of doubt, then no hadd and nothing for ifda', but the dower (uqr) is due. If she was coerced without a claim of doubt, then he receives the hadd and not her, and she has no dower. Then consider the ifda': if her urine does not hold, he must pay the full diyah of a woman because he destroyed the type of benefit completely; if her urine holds, he receives the hadd and must pay one-third of the diyah because his injury is a penetrating wound (ja'ifah). If there is a claim of doubt, then no hadd on either. If the urine holds, he must pay one-third of the diyah and the dower is due according to the apparent narration; if it does not hold, he must pay the full diyah and the dower is not due according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. If she was a minor who is normally subject to intercourse, she is like an adult in what we mentioned, except regarding the dropping of the compensatory payment (arsh) due to her consent. If she is a minor who is not normally subject to intercourse, then if her urine holds, he must pay one-third of the diyah and the full dower, and there is no hadd due to the deficiency in the meaning of zina, which is insertion into the desired vulva; for this reason, the prohibition of affinity is not established. Unlawful intercourse in the Abode of Islam necessitates the dower if the hadd is negated; so one-third of the diyah is due because it is a penetrating wound, as we explained. If her urine does not hold, he is liable for the diyah and does not owe the dower according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He owes the dower as well for the reason mentioned. For us, the diyah covers the entire organ and the dower covers a part of it; the guarantee of a part is included in the guarantee of the whole when they are in the same organ, just as if one cuts a person's finger then cuts his hand before healing, the compensation for the finger enters into the compensation for the hand. His ihsan (status of being muhsan) is dropped by this intercourse due to the existence of the form of zina, which is unlawful intercourse. In al-Muhit: If he breaks a woman's thigh during zina or wounds her, he is liable for the diyah from his own wealth alone because it is quasi-intentional; in a case of doubt, the diyah is due from his wealth, meaning thereby for injuries less than life. If the slave commits a crime and then zina is committed with her, Allah says: 'The female and male fornicators, flog each of them...' [24:2]... the meaning that shows the act of zina with his saying 'I commit zina with you' is not flogged along with the word 'dower' contradicts it. End. And he affirmed it in al-Nahr.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the ruling concerning a person who commits zina with a female slave and kills her during the act. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that both the hadd punishment and the payment of the slave's value are obligatory, unless the caliph is involved—then the caliph is subject to retaliation and financial penalties but not hadd. The key issue is whether the obligation to pay the value creates a right of ownership that drops the hadd. Abu Yusuf argues that it does, drawing an analogy with purchasing the slave after zina. But Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the guarantee here is for killing, not for the usufruct, and ownership does not arise retroactively for consumed benefits. The text then explores various scenarios: zina with a free woman leading to death, causing ifda' (infibulation) to a woman with or without her consent, and cases with minors. Detailed diyah amounts are given based on whether urination is controlled. The author also addresses the effect on ihsan (muhsan status). The passage includes a reference to a Quranic verse and a brief comment from al-Muhit on injuries during zina. The overall structure follows the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt that prevents the application of the hadd penalty. In this passage, a claim of doubt (like a marriage contract) negates the hadd.
إفضاء (ifda'): Physical injury causing the fusion or piercing of the urinary and reproductive tracts, often resulting in incontinence.
عقر (uqr): The dower (mahr) paid for sexual intercourse in cases where the regular marriage contract is absent, especially when there is a shubhah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (as per the text), what is the ruling if a person commits zina with a female slave and then kills her during the act?
A) Only the hadd is due, no financial compensation.
B) Both the hadd and the value of the slave are due.
C) Only the value is due because the hadd is dropped due to ownership.
D) The hadd is due only if the slave was not killed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, combined criminal and financial penalties are both applied for distinct crimes, and payment of value does not create retroactive ownership to drop the hadd.

Ifda' and Shubhah: Detailed Rulings on Zina Causing Injury
Expansion on ifda' and shubhah in zina cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings for ifda' (perforation) with and without shubhah, and calculate the diyah amounts based on urine control.

Core Idea
The ruling for ifda' depends on consent, shubhah, and the extent of injury; full diyah for total loss of control, one-third diyah for a penetrating wound.

The passage continues with detailed scenarios where zina leads to ifda' (perforation of tracts) rather than death. The author outlines the rulings for adult women, minors, and the effect of shubhah. This section also addresses the interaction between dower (uqr) and diyah, including an intra-Hanafi dispute between Muhammad and the two elders.

Guided Path
1
Identify the injury (ifda') and variables
Ifda' is the piercing of the urinary and reproductive tracts. The ruling depends on consent (willing vs coerced), presence of shubhah (claim of doubt), and the resulting incontinence (urine holds or not). For minors, also consider whether she is normally subject to intercourse.
2
Apply the rule for an adult willing woman with no shubhah
Both receive hadd. No compensation for ifda' due to her consent. No dower because hadd is due.
Consent does not avoid hadd for zina.
3
Apply the rule if there is a claim of shubhah
No hadd. Uqr (dower) is due. For ifda', determine diyah based on urine control: if urine holds, one-third diyah; if not, full diyah.
Shubhah drops the hadd and triggers financial obligations.
4
Apply the rule for a coerced woman with no shubhah
Man receives hadd, woman does not. No dower. For ifda', if urine does not hold, full diyah; if it holds, hadd plus one-third diyah.
Coercion removes hadd from the woman but not from the man.
5
Handle minors and the intra-Hanafi dispute
Minors who are normally subject to intercourse are treated like adults, except that her consent does not drop compensation (arsh). For minors not normally subject, no hadd due to deficiency in the meaning of zina, but diyah and uqr are due. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no uqr when full diyah is paid; Muhammad says uqr is due even with full diyah.
The dispute: whether compensation for a part (uqr) is included in compensation for the whole (diyah).

Source Text

لمحمد وإن كانت صغيرة يجامع مثلها فهي كالكبيرة فيما ذكرنا إلا في حق سقوط الأرش برضاها، وإن كانت صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها، فإن كان يستمسك بولها لزمه ثلث الدية والمهر كاملاً ولا حد عليه لتمكن القصور في معنى الزنا وهو الإيلاج في قبل المشتهاة، ولهذا لا تثبت به حرمة المصاهرة والوطء الحرام في دار الإسلام يوجب المهر إذا انتفى الحد فيجب ثلث الدية لكونه جائفة على ما بينا، وإن كان لا يستمسك ضمن الدية ولا يضمن المهر عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد: يضمن المهر أيضاً لما ذكرنا ولنا أن الدية ضمان كل العضو والمهر ضمان جزء منه وضمان الجزء يدخل في ضمان الكل إذا كانا في عضو واحد كما إذا قطع أصبع إنسان ثم قطع كفته قبل البرء يدخل أرش الأصبع في أرش الكف ويسقط إحصانه بهذا الوطء لوجود صورة الزنا وهو الوطء الحرام. وفي المحيط : لو كسر فخذ امرأة في الزنا أو جرحها ضمن الدية في ماله وحده لأنه شبه العمد وفي شبهة تجب الدية في ماله يعني به فيما دون النفس، وإن جنت الأمة فزني بها قال الله تعالى الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا [النور: ۲] فالمعنى الذي يفيد أن فعل الزنا مع قوله أزني بك لا يجلد معه للفظ المهر معارض له اهـ. وأقره في النهر .
The Book of Hudud: Chapter on Intercourse that Incurs the Hadd and That Which Does Not. He committed zina with a female slave and killed her; both the hadd and the value are incumbent upon him. The caliph is subject to retaliation and financial penalties, not hadd. The meaning of value is that he killed her by the act of zina because he committed two crimes, so the ruling for each is applied in full. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he is not subject to hadd because the establishment of liability for the value is a cause for ownership of the slave, and it becomes as if he purchased her after having committed zina with her. This is based on the dispute and the objection that a cause of ownership before the establishment of hadd necessitates its dropping, as when one owns stolen property before amputation. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is a guarantee for killing, not ownership, because the guarantee that necessitates ownership only necessitates it in the commodity, as in a gift of stolen property, not in the usufruct of sexual intercourse because it has been enjoyed, and ownership is established retroactively, so it does not appear in what has been consumed because it is non-existent. This is unlike the case where he committed zina with her and then destroyed her eye, where he must pay her value and the hadd is dropped, because ownership there is established in the physical body, which is a commodity, so it creates doubt. The author indicated that if he committed zina with a free woman and killed her as a result, the hadd is incumbent on him by agreement, because a free woman is not owned by the guarantee. If he did not kill her but rather caused ifda' (perforation of the urinary and reproductive tracts), then if she was an adult, willing, and without a claim of doubt, both receive the hadd, and nothing is required from him for the ifda' due to her consent, and no dower is due because of the hadd. If there is a claim of doubt, then no hadd and nothing for ifda', but the dower (uqr) is due. If she was coerced without a claim of doubt, then he receives the hadd and not her, and she has no dower. Then consider the ifda': if her urine does not hold, he must pay the full diyah of a woman because he destroyed the type of benefit completely; if her urine holds, he receives the hadd and must pay one-third of the diyah because his injury is a penetrating wound (ja'ifah). If there is a claim of doubt, then no hadd on either. If the urine holds, he must pay one-third of the diyah and the dower is due according to the apparent narration; if it does not hold, he must pay the full diyah and the dower is not due according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. If she was a minor who is normally subject to intercourse, she is like an adult in what we mentioned, except regarding the dropping of the compensatory payment (arsh) due to her consent. If she is a minor who is not normally subject to intercourse, then if her urine holds, he must pay one-third of the diyah and the full dower, and there is no hadd due to the deficiency in the meaning of zina, which is insertion into the desired vulva; for this reason, the prohibition of affinity is not established. Unlawful intercourse in the Abode of Islam necessitates the dower if the hadd is negated; so one-third of the diyah is due because it is a penetrating wound, as we explained. If her urine does not hold, he is liable for the diyah and does not owe the dower according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He owes the dower as well for the reason mentioned. For us, the diyah covers the entire organ and the dower covers a part of it; the guarantee of a part is included in the guarantee of the whole when they are in the same organ, just as if one cuts a person's finger then cuts his hand before healing, the compensation for the finger enters into the compensation for the hand. His ihsan (status of being muhsan) is dropped by this intercourse due to the existence of the form of zina, which is unlawful intercourse. In al-Muhit: If he breaks a woman's thigh during zina or wounds her, he is liable for the diyah from his own wealth alone because it is quasi-intentional; in a case of doubt, the diyah is due from his wealth, meaning thereby for injuries less than life. If the slave commits a crime and then zina is committed with her, Allah says: 'The female and male fornicators, flog each of them...' [24:2]... the meaning that shows the act of zina with his saying 'I commit zina with you' is not flogged along with the word 'dower' contradicts it. End. And he affirmed it in al-Nahr.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the ruling concerning a person who commits zina with a female slave and kills her during the act. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that both the hadd punishment and the payment of the slave's value are obligatory, unless the caliph is involved—then the caliph is subject to retaliation and financial penalties but not hadd. The key issue is whether the obligation to pay the value creates a right of ownership that drops the hadd. Abu Yusuf argues that it does, drawing an analogy with purchasing the slave after zina. But Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the guarantee here is for killing, not for the usufruct, and ownership does not arise retroactively for consumed benefits. The text then explores various scenarios: zina with a free woman leading to death, causing ifda' (infibulation) to a woman with or without her consent, and cases with minors. Detailed diyah amounts are given based on whether urination is controlled. The author also addresses the effect on ihsan (muhsan status). The passage includes a reference to a Quranic verse and a brief comment from al-Muhit on injuries during zina. The overall structure follows the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary.

Key Terms
إفضاء (ifda'): Physical injury causing the fusion or piercing of the urinary and reproductive tracts, often resulting in incontinence.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt that prevents the application of the hadd penalty. In this passage, a claim of doubt (like a marriage contract) negates the hadd.
عقر (uqr): The dower (mahr) paid for sexual intercourse in cases where the regular marriage contract is absent, especially when there is a shubhah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a man causes ifda' to a free woman with total incontinence, and there is no shubhah, what must he pay?
A) Full diyah only.
B) Full diyah and dower.
C) One-third diyah only.
D) Hadd only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grades compensation for ifda' based on the loss of bodily function, and the dower is not due when full diyah is paid.

The Caliph's Liability: Qisas Applies, Hudud Do Not
Ruling on the caliph's liability for qisas and hudud with reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the caliph's liability for qisas and hudud, and explain the rationale based on the distinction between huquq al-ibad and huquq Allah.

Core Idea
The caliph is subject to qisas (rights of individuals) but immune from hudud (rights of God) because no one has authority over him.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a fundamental legal question: can the supreme ruler be punished? The Hanafi position draws a sharp distinction between penalties that are rights of individuals (qisas) and those that are rights of God (hudud). Understanding this ruling is crucial for grasping the limits of state authority in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize that the passage separates penalties into qisas (and financial penalties) on one hand and hudud on the other. The caliph is treated differently for each.
2
Understand the legal basis for each
Qisas is a right of the individual (haqq al-ibad); hudud is a right of God (haqq Allah). This distinction determines liability.
3
Analyze the impossibility argument for hudud
The caliph is the executor of hudud; no one has authority over him. It is impossible for him to execute the punishment on himself. Therefore, the obligation drops.
This is a practical impossibility, not a claim of legal immunity in principle.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
The term 'caliph' refers to the supreme imam with no superior. Lower governors (amir al-balda) are not exempt; they can receive hudud by order of the caliph.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخليفة يؤخذ بالقصاص والأموال لا بالحد لأن الأول حقوق العباد لما أن حق استيفائها لمن له الحق فيكون الإمام فيه كغيره وإن احتاج إلى المنعة فالمسلمون منعته فيقدر بهم على الاستيفاء فكان الوجوب مفيداً، وبهذا يعلم أنه يجوز استيفاء القصاص بدون قضاء القاضي والقضاء لتمكين الولي من استيفائه لا أنه شرط كما صرحوا به. وأما الثاني - أعني الحدود ـ فإنما لا تقام عليه لأن الحد حق الله تعالى والإمام هو المكلف بإقامته وتعذر إقامته على نفسه لأن إقامته بطريق الجزاء والنكال ولا يفعل ذلك أحد بنفسه ولا ولاية لأحد عليه ليستوفيه وفائدة الإيجاب الاستيفاء فإذا تعذر لم يجب وفعل نائبه كفعله لأنه بأمره أطلق في الحد فشمل حد القذف لأن المغلب فيه حق الشرع فكان كبقية الحدود والمراد بالخليفة الإمام الذي ليس فوقه إمام، وقيد به احترازاً عن أمير البلدة فإنه يقام عليه الحدود بأمر الإمام والله أعلم.
And the caliph is taken to account for qisas and financial penalties, not for hadd penalties. Because the former are rights of the people, since the right to execute them belongs to the one who has the right, so the imam is like others in that. Even if he needs support, the Muslims support him, so he is able to execute through them; thus the obligation is beneficial. And by this it is known that it is permissible to execute qisas without a judge's ruling, and the ruling is to enable the guardian to execute, not a condition as they stated. As for the second - meaning the hudud - they are not executed upon him because the hadd is a right of God, and the imam is charged with executing it, and it is impossible for him to execute it on himself because its execution is by way of punishment and deterrence, and no one does that to himself, nor does anyone have authority over him to execute it. And the benefit of obligation is execution, so when it is impossible, it is not obligatory. And the act of his deputy is like his act because it is by his command. It is general for hudud, including hadd of qadhf because the dominant aspect is the right of the shari'ah, so it is like other hudud. And by 'caliph' is meant the imam who has no imam above him. It is restricted to differentiate from the governor of a city, for hudud are executed upon him by order of the imam. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage states a key legal distinction: the caliph (supreme ruler) is subject to qisas (retaliation) and financial penalties because these are rights of individuals (huquq al-ibad) that can be claimed by the victim or their heirs. However, he is not subject to hadd penalties (e.g., lashing, stoning) because hudud are rights of God, and the caliph is the one responsible for executing them. It is logically impossible for him to execute a hadd on himself, and no one has authority over him to do so. The passage also clarifies that the caliph's deputy can act on his behalf, and that this ruling applies even to hadd al-qadhf because it is predominantly a divine right. Importantly, the immunity is for the supreme caliph, not for lower governors who can be subjected to hudud by the caliph's order. The commentary also notes that qisas can be carried out without a judge's ruling, though a judge's ruling facilitates it.

Key Terms
خليفة (khalifah): The supreme imam (ruler) with no authority above him; the head of the Islamic state.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation or prescribed punishment for murder or bodily harm, considered a right of the victim/guardians.
حد (hadd): A fixed penalty prescribed by God (e.g., lashing for zina, drinking, theft, qadhf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the caliph not subject to hadd penalties according to this passage?
A) Because the hadd is a right of God and the caliph is above God's law
B) Because the caliph is the one responsible for executing hudud and no one has authority to execute it on him
C) Because hudud only apply to common people
D) Because the caliph can always repent and avoid hadd

Key Takeaway
The caliph's immunity from hudud is due to practical impossibility, but he remains fully accountable for private rights (qisas and financial claims).

The Unknown Woman in Zina: Confession vs. Testimony
Explains the distinction between confession and testimony when the woman is unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between confession and testimony when the woman in a zina case is unknown, and apply the principle of dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat.

Core Idea
Shubha (ambiguity) prevents hadd; confession reveals certainty, testimony leaves doubt.

In Hanafi hudud, the application of hadd for zina is strictly conditioned on certainty. When a man confesses to zina with an unknown woman, he knows whether she was lawful to him; thus his confession removes ambiguity. But when witnesses testify against a man for zina with an unknown woman, the possibility that she was his wife or slavegirl creates a shubha that blocks the hadd. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Confession vs. testimony when the woman is unknown. Note the ruling for each.
2
Note the ruling difference
Confession incurs hadd; testimony does not.
3
Locate the underlying rationale
Shubha (ambiguity) in testimony; no shubha in confession because the confessor knows her status.
4
Examine the dalil
The Prophet stoned Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah when they confessed with absent partners, showing that absence of the partner does not remove the hadd in confession.
5
Understand the shubha hierarchy
Actual shubha (e.g., retraction) blocks hadd; but mere possibility of shubha (shubha of shubha) does not.
Distinguish between real shubha and speculative shubha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أقر بالزنا بمجهولة حد وإن شهدوا بذلك لا كاختلافهم في طوعها أو في البلد ولو على كل زنا أربعة ولو اختلفوا في بيت واحد حد الرجل سرق وهو فلان غائب لم يقطع، والفرق أن بالغيبة تنعدم الدعوى وهي شرط في السرقة من دون الزنا، وبالحضور يتوهم دعوى الشبهة ولا معتبر بالموهوم لأنه شبهة الشبهة واعتبارها يؤدي إلى سد باب الحدود لأن المقر يحتمل أن يرجع فرجوعه شبهة فيدرأ به الحد، واحتمال رجوعه شبهة الشبهة فلا يسقط، وكذا البينة يحتمل رجوعها فرجوعها حقيقة شبهة واحتماله شبهة الشبهة. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو أقر أنه زنى بفلانة وهي غائبة فإنه يحد بالأولى، ولأنه عليه السلام رجم ماعزاً، والغامدية حين أقر بالزنا بغائبين وقيد بالزنا لأنه لو كان القصاص بين شريكين وكان أحدهما غائباً لا يتمكن الحاضر من الاستيفاء لاحتمال العفو من الغائب وهو حقيقة المسقط، فاحتماله يكون شبهة المسقط لا شبهة الشبهة قوله : (وإن أقر بالزنا بمجهولة حد وإن شهدوا بذلك (لا أي شهدوا عليه أنه زنى بامرأة لا يعرفونها لا يحد لاحتمال أنها امرأته أو أمته هو الظاهر بخلاف الإقرار لأنه لا يخفى عليه امرأته وأمته، ولا اعتبار باحتمال أن تكون أمته بالميراث ولا يعرفها لأنه ثابت في المعروفة كالمجهولة واعتباره يؤدي إلى انسداد باب الحدود. وفي كافي الحاكم الشهيد وإن قال المشهود عليه إن التي رأوها معي ليست لي بامرأة ولا خادم لم يحد أيضاً، وذلك لأنها يتصور أنها أمة ابنه أو منكوحة نكاحاً فاسداً .اهـ. وهذا التعليل أولى مما علل به لعدم الوجوب من أنه إقرار مرة واحدة لأنه يقتضي أنه لو قال هذه المقالة أربعاً حد وليس كذلك. وفي الخانية : لو قالوا زنى بامرأة لا نعرفها ثم قالوا بفلانة فإنه لا يحد الرجل ولا الشهود اهـ.
And if he confesses to zina with an unknown woman, he is hadded; but if they testify to that, no (i.e., they are not hadded). The distinction is that with absence [of the woman], the claim is non-existent and it is a condition in theft not in zina, and with presence the claim of ambiguity is conjectured and conjecture is not considered because it is an ambiguity of ambiguity. Considering it would lead to closing the door of hudud because the confessing one may retract, and his retraction is an ambiguity, so hadd is repelled by it. The possibility of his retraction is an ambiguity of ambiguity, so it does not drop. Similarly, the evidence may retract, their actual retraction is an ambiguity, and its possibility is an ambiguity of ambiguity. The author indicated that if he confessed that he committed zina with so-and-so while she is absent, he is hadded a fortiori. And because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stoned Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyyah when they confessed to zina with absent persons. It is restricted to zina because if it were retaliation between partners and one of them was absent, the present one cannot execute retaliation due to the possibility of pardon from the absent one, which is a real cause of dropping, so its possibility becomes an ambiguity of the dropper, not an ambiguity of ambiguity. His statement: 'And if he confesses to zina with an unknown woman, he is hadded; but if they testify to that, no' means if they testify that he committed zina with a woman they do not know, he is not hadded due to the possibility that she may be his wife or his slavegirl. That is apparent, unlike confession because it is not hidden from him his wife and his slavegirl. And no consideration is given to the possibility that she may be his slavegirl by inheritance and he does not know her, because that is established in the known as well as the unknown, and considering it leads to closing the door of hudud. In the Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid: If the one testified against says that the woman they saw with me is neither my wife nor my servant, he is also not hadded, because it is conceivable that she is the slavegirl of his son or one married in a fasid marriage. This reasoning is more appropriate than the reasoning for lack of obligation that it is a single confession, because it implies that if he said this statement four times, he would be hadded, which is not the case. In al-Khaniyyah: If they said he committed zina with a woman they do not know, then they said with so-and-so, then he is not hadded and neither are the witnesses.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from Al-Bahr al-Raiq on the topic of testimony of zina. The author distinguishes between confession and testimony when the woman is unknown. In a confession, the confessor knows whether the woman is lawful for him or not, so if he confesses to zina with an unknown woman, he is punished with hadd because he knows the reality. However, witnesses who testify to zina with an unknown woman do not cause the man to be hadded, because it is possible that the woman is his wife or his slavegirl, which would make the act lawful. The presumption of ambiguity (shubha) prevents the hadd. The text also discusses the nuance: even if the accused says the woman is not his wife or servant, he is not hadded because she could be the slavegirl of his son or a woman in a fasid marriage. The reasoning that it is a single confession (which would not require the full four confessions) is rejected because the law requires four confessions for the hadd to be established, but here it is about testimony, not confession. The passage also references the Kafi and al-Khaniyyah for further details.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): An ambiguity that raises doubt about the applicability of hadd, thereby preventing its execution.
درء الحدود بالشبهات (dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat): The legal maxim that hudud punishments are to be repelled by any plausible ambiguity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if witnesses testify that a man committed zina with a woman they do not know?
A) The man is hadded.
B) The man is not hadded.
C) The witnesses are hadded for qadhf.
D) The man is hadded only if he confesses.

Key Takeaway
The hadd for zina is blocked by any plausible shubha, even a remote one, unless the accused eliminates it through confession.

Disagreement on Consent in Zina Testimony
Intra-Hanafi dispute on consent disagreement in zina testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on consent disagreement and explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Disagreement on consent creates doubt that removes hadd from both parties according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

The testimony in zina cases requires four witnesses agreeing on all details. When witnesses disagree on whether the woman consented or was coerced, the hadd punishment is affected. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on this issue, highlighting how the legal reasoning shapes the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The witnesses disagree on the woman's consent: two say she was coerced, two say she consented. Determine the legal effect on hadd for both parties.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam holds that no hadd applies to either the man or the woman because zina is a single act and the consent witnesses become defamers (qadhin) of the woman.
Key: witnesses of consent are essentially accusing her of adultery without four witnesses, so their testimony is invalid against her.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only the man is hadded because all four agree on his act, and the extra element (coercion) does not negate the agreement.
They see the disagreement as affecting only the woman's side.
4
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
Imam's response: the witnesses of consent are essentially accusing the woman, so they need four witnesses to prove zina against her; lacking that, they become qadhin themselves and their testimony cannot support hadd on her.
This reasoning also addresses the scenario where three testify to consent and one to coercion.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam's view, neither is punished; under Sahibayn, only the man is punished. The practical consequence is significant for the woman's legal outcome.
The mufta bihi is Imam's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (كاختلافهم في طوعها أو في البلد ولو على كل زنا أربعة) بيان لمسألتين لا حد فيهما: الأولى لو اختلف الشهود في طوع المرأة فشهد اثنان أنه استكرهها واثنان أنها طاوعته وعدم وجوب الحد عليهما قول الإمام. وقالا: يحد الرجل خاصة لاتفاقهم على الموجب عليه راد أحد الفريقين بزيادة جناية وهو الإكراه بخلاف جانبها لأن طواعيتها شرط لتحقق الموجب في حقها ولم يثبت لاختلافهم وله أنه اختلف المشهود عليه لأن الزنا فعل واحد يقوم بهما ولأن شاهدي الطواعية صارا قاذفين لها، وإنما يسقط الحد عنهما لشهادة شاهدي الإكراه لأن زناها مكرهة يسقط إحصانها فصارا خصمين في ذلك أطلقه فشمل ما إذا شهد ثلاثة بالطواعية وواحد بالإكراه وعكسه لكن في الوجه الأول يحد الثلاثة حد القذف لعدم سقوط إحصانها بشهادة الفرد وعند الإمام لا يحدون في الوجوه الثلاثة لأن اتفاق الأربعة على النسبة إلى الزنا بلفظ الشهادة مخرج لكلامهم من أن يكون قذفاً. الثانية لو اختلفوا في البلد الذي وقع فيها الزنا فهو على وجهين: أحدهما أن يشهد اثنان أنه زنى بها بالكوفة واثنان أنه زنى بها بالبصرة فلا حد عليهما لأن المشهود به فعل الزنا وقد اختلف باختلاف المكان ولم يتم على كل واحد منهما نصاب الشهادة ولا يحد الشهود خلافاً لزفر لشبهة الاتحاد نظراً إلى اتحاد الصورة والمرأة. وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا جاء القاذف بأربعة شهداء فشهد اثنان أنه زنى في بلد وآخران أنه زنى في بلد آخر. وثانيهما أن يتم نصاب الشهادة بالزنا في كل بلد وهو على وجهين أحدهما أن يذكروا وقتاً واحداً تباعد المكانين كما إذا شهد أربعة أنه زنى بها بالبصرة وقت طلوع الشمس في اليوم الفلاني في الشهر الفلاني السنة الفلانية وأربعة أنه زنى بها بالكوفة في الوقت المذكور بعينه، وفي هذه لا حد عليهما وهو المراد بقوله ولو على كل زنا أربعة» لتيقننا بكذب أحدهما لأن الشخص الواحد لا يكون في ساعة واحدة في مكانين متباعدين، ولا يعرف الصادق من الكاذب فيعجز القاضي عن الحكم بهما للتعارض أو لتهمة الكذب ولا يحد الشهود أيضاً لأن كل واحد منهما تم به نصاب الشهادة واحتمل الصدق ثانيهما أن يتقارب المكانان مع اتحاد الوقت فتجوز شهادتهم لأنه يصح كون الأمر فيهما في ذلك الوقت لأن طلوع الشمس يقال لوقت ممتد امتداداً عرفياً لا أنه يخص وقت ظهورها من الأفق ويحتمل تكرار الفعل؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وذكر الحاكم في كافيه : إذا شهد أربعة على رجل بالزنا فاختلفوا في المزني بها أو في المكان أو في الوقت بطلت شهادتهم إلا أن يكون اختلافهم في مكانين متقاربين من بيت أو غير بيت فيقام الحد استحساناً اهـ
His statement: 'Like their disagreement on her consent or on the city, even if there are four for each act of zina' is an explanation of two issues in which there is no hadd. First: If the witnesses disagree on the woman's consent: two testify that he coerced her and two that she consented. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no hadd on either of them. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say: only the man is hadded, because they all agree on the obligation upon him, and one group adds an extra offense (coercion). As for the woman, her consent is a condition for the obligation in her right, and it is not established due to their disagreement. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the one testified against is disputed, because zina is a single act involving both; also, the two witnesses of consent have become defamers (qadhin) of her, and they are saved from hadd only by the testimony of the coercion witnesses, because her zina under coercion drops her ihsan. This is general, including if three testify to consent and one to coercion, and vice versa. But in the first case, the three are hadded for qadhf because her ihsan is not dropped by one witness; according to Imam, they are not hadded in all three cases because the agreement of the four on attributing zina through the wording of testimony removes their speech from being qadhf. Second, disagreement on the city where zina occurred has two aspects. One: two testify Kufa, two Basra: no hadd on either, because the testified act is zina and it differs by location, and the full complement of testimony is not completed for each; the witnesses are not hadded, contrary to Zufar, because of the semblance of unity considering the unity of the act and the woman. The same disagreement applies if a defamer brings four witnesses and two testify to one city and two to another. The second aspect is that the full complement is completed for each city: this has two subcases. First: they mention a single time but distant places, e.g., four testify to Basra at sunrise on a specific date and four to Kufa at the same time: in this case, no hadd on either, because we are certain one is lying; the judge cannot determine which, so he cannot judge; the witnesses are also not hadded because the full complement is completed for each and truth is possible. Second: the places are close together and the time is the same: their testimony is accepted, because it is possible that the act occurred in both places at that time (sunrise is an extended period), and it is possible the act was repeated. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. Al-Hakim in his Kafi says: If four testify against a man for zina and they differ on the woman, the place, or the time, their testimony is void, unless their difference is on two close places (e.g., within a house), in which case hadd is imposed by istihsan.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab (intra-Hanafi) dispute and ruling. It covers two issues: first, disagreement on consent (taw' / ikrah). Imam Abu Hanifa holds no hadd on either party because the act is one and the consent witnesses become qadhin. The Sahibayn say only the man is hadded because they agree on his act. The second issue is disagreement on the location (balad). If two witnesses say Kufa and two say Basra, no hadd because the testimony is incomplete for each location. If four testify to each city but at the same time in distant places, the testimony is contradictory and invalid because one set must be lying. However, if the places are close (like adjacent areas), hadd is imposed by istihsan because the act could have spanned both. The passage also discusses nuances like the case of three vs one on consent, and the ruling when the accused is present.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion; in zina, it removes the obligation of hadd on the woman.
طواعية (tawa'iyyah): Consent; it is a condition for hadd on the woman in zina.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; punishable by hadd of eighty lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if two witnesses testify that a man coerced a woman into zina and two testify that she consented, what is the ruling?
A) Both man and woman are punished.
B) Only the man is punished.
C) Neither is punished.
D) Only the woman is punished.

Key Takeaway
Disagreement on consent in zina testimony removes hadd from both parties according to Imam Abu Hanifa's relied-upon position.

Disagreement on Location in Zina Testimony
Ruling on location disagreement in zina testimony with two subcases and Zufar's opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on location disagreement to determine when hadd is imposed or dropped.

Core Idea
Disagreement on the location of zina can invalidate testimony, but if places are close, hadd is imposed by istihsan.

When witnesses disagree on the location where zina occurred, the validity of their testimony depends on whether the full complement of witnesses is completed for each location and whether the locations are compatible. This lesson covers two scenarios: incomplete testimony (two vs two) and complete but contradictory testimony (four vs four at distant or close locations).

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario
Two witnesses say Kufa, two say Basra. The testimony for each location is incomplete. Determine the ruling on hadd and on the witnesses.
No hadd on the accused, and witnesses are not hadded contrary to Zufar.
2
Identify the second scenario
There are four witnesses for each location (e.g., four say Kufa, four say Basra) at the same time. If locations are distant, the testimony is contradictory.
One set must be lying; judge cannot know which, so no hadd on accused, and witnesses not hadded because each set has a full complement and could be truthful.
3
Apply the close-location exception
If the locations are close (e.g., within a house), testimony is accepted and hadd is imposed by istihsan, because the act could have spanned both places.
Also consider the possibility of repeated acts.
4
Note the disagreement with Zufar
Zufar holds that in the first scenario (two+two), the witnesses should be hadded for qadhf because they did not complete the testimony for a single location. The Hanafi school rejects this due to shubha of unity.
The Hanafi position is that the witnesses are not hadded.
5
Understand the overall principle
The key is that the testimony must be complete and consistent on the essential details (location, time, woman) for hadd to be imposed. Inconsistency on location can be reconciled if the places are close.
This illustrates the importance of tawatur (consistency) in testimony requirements.

وقالا: يحد الرجل خاصة لاتفاقهم على الموجب عليه راد أحد الفريقين بزيادة جناية وهو الإكراه بخلاف جانبها لأن طواعيتها شرط لتحقق الموجب في حقها ولم يثبت لاختلافهم وله أنه اختلف المشهود عليه لأن الزنا فعل Disagreement on Spot within One House: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Explains the istihsan ruling when witnesses differ on the corner within a small house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when witnesses differ on the exact spot within a small house for zina and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
When witnesses disagree on the exact corner within a small house, hadd is still imposed because reconciliation is possible.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a subtle point in the law of testimony for hudud. The general rule is that disagreement on the place of zina invalidates testimony and prevents hadd. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan when the disagreement is within a small house, because the difference can be reconciled without contradiction. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this exception, including a distinction between qiyas and istihsan, and addresses a related objection regarding coercion and consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sides of the argument
Contrast qiyas (no hadd) with istihsan (hadd imposed). Note the general rule and the exception.
Qiyas compares to disagreement on separate houses or cities.
2
Understand the illa of reconciliation (tawfiq)
The key to istihsan is the possibility of reconciling the testimonies. What makes reconciliation possible within a small house vs. not in large houses or separate houses?
Movement can cover a small house but not a large one.
3
Apply the distinction between small and large houses
The exception is restricted to small houses. Large houses are treated like separate dwellings. Consider the rationale: a large house (dar) is like two separate properties.
Al-Bahr al-Raiq restricts 'bayt' to a small house.
4
Evaluate the objection regarding coercion and consent
The author raises an ishkal: why not apply similar reconciliation to disagreement on coercion vs. consent? The response from Al-Kafi shows that the starting point (coercion) negates hadd, creating doubt, whereas in the corner case both starting points still require hadd.
Distinguish between reconcilable details and elements that change the legal nature of the act.
5
Summarize the ruling and its basis
State the final ruling: hadd is imposed by istihsan. The principle is that when reconciliation is possible, apparent disagreement does not invalidate testimony.
This is an application of the Hanafi concept of tawfiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو اختلفوا في بيت واحد حد الرجل والمرأة) أي اختلفوا في مكان الزنا من بيت واحد كما إذا شهد اثنان أنه زنى بها في زاوية منه واثنان أنه زنى بها في زاوية أخرى منه وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يجب لاختلاف المكان حقيقة. وجه الاستحسان أن التوفيق ممكن بأن يكون ابتداء الفعل في زاوية والانتهاء في زاوية أخرى بالاضطراب والحركة أو لأن الواقع في وسط البيت فيحسبه من في المقدم في المقدم ومن في المؤخر في المؤخر فيشهد بحسب ما عنده . أطلق في البيت وهو مقيد بالصغير لأن الكبير كالدار ولو اختلفا في دارين لا حد كالبلدين والحاصل أن الاختلاف في المكان مانع لقبولها إلا إذا أمكن التوفيق بأن يكون صغيراً. وقيد الاختلاف بما ذكر لأنهم لو اختلفوا في طولها وقصرها أو سمنها أو هزالها أو في لونها أو في ثيابها فإنه لا يمنع لإمكان التوفيق. وقد استشكل على هذا مذهب الإمام فيما إذا اختلفوا في الإكراه والطواعية فإن التوفيق فيه ممكن بأن يكون ابتداء الفعل كرهاً وانتهاؤه طواعية. قال في الكافي : يمكن أن يجاب عنه بأن ابتداء الفعل إذا كان عن إكراه لا يوجب الحد فبالنظر إلى الابتداء لا يجب وبالنظر إلى الانتهاء يجب فلا يجب بالشك، وهنا بالنظر إلى الزاويتين يجب فافترقا .
His statement: 'And if they differ on a single house, the man and woman are hadded' means they differed on the place of zina within one house, e.g., two testified he committed zina in one corner and two in another corner. This is istihsan; by qiyas, hadd should not be imposed because of the actual difference in place. The reason for istihsan is that reconciliation is possible: the act may have started in one corner and ended in another due to movement, or because someone in the front of the house perceives it as front and someone in the back as back. The word 'house' is restricted to a small house, because a large one is like a courtyard. If they differ on two houses, there is no hadd, like two cities. The conclusion is that disagreement on place prevents acceptance unless reconciliation is possible, as with a small house. The disagreement is restricted to what is mentioned, because if they differ on her height, short, fat, thin, color, or clothes, it does not prevent acceptance because reconciliation is possible. A difficulty was raised against Imam's view on disagreement on coercion and consent, since reconciliation is possible there too: the act could have started with coercion and ended with consent. The Kafi responds: the beginning of the act if under coercion does not require hadd, so with respect to the beginning it is not required, and with respect to the end it is required, so it is not required due to doubt. Here with respect to the two corners, it is required, so they differ.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Bahr al-Raiq. It addresses a specific case: witnesses differ on the exact corner within a small house where zina occurred. By qiyas (analogy to the case of different houses or cities), the disagreement should invalidate the testimony and preclude hadd. However, the ruling according to istihsan (juristic preference) is that both the man and woman are hadded. The reason is that reconciliation is possible: the act may have moved from one corner to another during the course of the act, or witnesses' perspectives may have differed. This applies only to a small house; if the house is large like a courtyard, it is treated like two separate dwellings. The passage also responds to a potential objection: why not apply similar reconciliation to the earlier case of disagreement on coercion vs consent? The answer is that coercion at the start negates hadd, whereas here both corners support the hadd; thus reconciliation leads to certainty, not doubt.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from qiyas to avoid hardship or achieve a better outcome.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an established case to a new case based on a common effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if witnesses differ on whether zina occurred in the front or back corner of a small house, what is the ruling?
A) No hadd due to disagreement.
B) Hadd is imposed by istihsan.
C) The witnesses are punished for qadhf.
D) Only the man is hadded.

Key Takeaway
When testimony differs on a reconcilable detail like the exact corner within a small house, hadd is still imposed by istihsan, overriding qiyas.

intermediate

Witness Disagreement on Location in Zina Cases
Explains rulings when witnesses for zina disagree on location

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when witnesses for zina disagree on the location of the act and apply the principle of shubhat al-ittihad to determine whether witnesses are punished.

Core Idea
When witnesses disagree on location, hadd is imposed only if testimonies can be reconciled; otherwise, no punishment on accused or witnesses.

In zina cases, the testimony of four witnesses is required for the imposition of hadd. But what happens when witnesses agree on the act but disagree on where it occurred? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the nuanced Hanafi position, distinguishing between scenarios where the testimonies can be reconciled and those where they cannot. Through this lesson, you will learn how the Hanafi school applies the concept of shubhat al-ittihad to protect witnesses from qadhf punishment while preserving the integrity of the hudud system.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Main Scenarios
The passage first presents a scenario where two witnesses claim the act in Kufa and two in Basra – each group lacks the nisab. Then a scenario where full nisab is achieved in each city (four witnesses each). Recognize the difference: incomplete vs complete nisab for each location.
In the first scenario, the total number of witnesses (four) is not split properly – the nisab is not complete for a single location.
2
Analyze the Ruling for the First Scenario (2+2 in Distant Cities)
In the first scenario, no hadd is imposed on the accused because the testimony is not complete for one act. Additionally, the witnesses are not punished for qadhf. Understand the reason: shubhat al-ittihad – the possibility that they all testify to the same act with the same woman creates doubt, protecting them from the hadd of qadhf.
Zufar dissents: he would punish the witnesses because the disagreement in place indicates falsehood.
3
Analyze the Second Scenario (Full Nisab in Each City) – Distant Places
When four witnesses testify to zina in Basra and four in Kufa at exactly the same time, the judge knows one group must be lying because a person cannot be in two distant places simultaneously. No hadd is imposed on the accused because the contradiction is irreconcilable. The witnesses are not punished because each group completed the nisab and could be truthful.
This is the meaning of the phrase 'even if for each zina there are four' – we are certain of falsehood but cannot identify the liars.
4
Analyze the Subcase of Close Places
If the two places are close (e.g., two rooms in the same house) and the time is the same, the testimonies are reconciled by istihsan. The time 'sunrise' is considered an extended time period, and it is possible for the act to have occurred in both places sequentially or with repetition. Hadd is imposed.
Al-Hakim's Kafi supports this: disagreement on place invalidates unless places are close, in which case hadd is imposed by istihsan.
5
Apply the Hanafi Principle of Reconciliation
The key distinction is whether the testimonies can be reconciled. If they can be interpreted as referring to the same act (through shubhat al-ittihad in the first scenario) or as possible due to closeness of place (second scenario subcase), hadd is imposed. If reconciliation is impossible (distant places, same time), hadd is dropped, and witnesses are not punished.
This principle prevents the hadd from falling into the category of shubha that would nullify it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البلد الذي وقع فيها الزنا فهو على وجهين: أحدهما أن يشهد اثنان أنه زنى بها بالكوفة واثنان أنه زنى بها بالبصرة فلا حد عليهما لأن المشهود به فعل الزنا وقد اختلف باختلاف المكان ولم يتم على كل واحد منهما نصاب الشهادة ولا يحد الشهود خلافاً لزفر لشبهة الاتحاد نظراً إلى اتحاد الصورة والمرأة. وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا جاء القاذف بأربعة شهداء فشهد اثنان أنه زنى في بلد وآخران أنه زنى في بلد آخر. وثانيهما أن يتم نصاب الشهادة بالزنا في كل بلد وهو على وجهين أحدهما أن يذكروا وقتاً واحداً تباعد المكانين كما إذا شهد أربعة أنه زنى بها بالبصرة وقت طلوع الشمس في اليوم الفلاني في الشهر الفلاني السنة الفلانية وأربعة أنه زنى بها بالكوفة في الوقت المذكور بعينه، وفي هذه لا حد عليهما وهو المراد بقوله "ولو على كل زنا أربعة" لتيقننا بكذب أحدهما لأن الشخص الواحد لا يكون في ساعة واحدة في مكانين متباعدين، ولا يعرف الصادق من الكاذب فيعجز القاضي عن الحكم بهما للتعارض أو لتهمة الكذب ولا يحد الشهود أيضاً لأن كل واحد منهما تم به نصاب الشهادة واحتمل الصدق ثانيهما أن يتقارب المكانان مع اتحاد الوقت فتجوز شهادتهم لأنه يصح كون الأمر فيهما في ذلك الوقت لأن طلوع الشمس يقال لوقت ممتد امتداداً عرفياً لا أنه يخص وقت ظهورها من الأفق ويحتمل تكرار الفعل؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وذكر الحاكم في كافيه : إذا شهد أربعة على رجل بالزنا فاختلفوا في المزني بها أو في المكان أو في الوقت بطلت شهادتهم إلا أن يكون اختلافهم في مكانين متقاربين من بيت أو غير بيت فيقام الحد استحساناً اهـ
The city in which the zina occurred has two aspects: First, two witnesses testify that he committed zina with her in Kufa and two testify that he committed zina with her in Basra, then there is no hadd on them because the testified act is zina and it differed by difference of place, and the required number of witnesses was not completed for each one; nor are the witnesses punished, contrary to Zufar, due to the semblance of unity considering the unity of the form and the woman. And on this disagreement is if the accuser brings four witnesses, so two testify that he committed zina in one city and another two that he committed zina in another city. Second, that the full number of witnesses for zina is completed in each city, and this has two aspects: First, that they mention one time while the two places are distant, such as if four witness that he committed zina with her in Basra at sunrise on such a day in such a month such a year, and four witness that he committed zina with her in Kufa at that exact same time; in this case there is no hadd on either, and that is intended by his saying 'even if for each zina there are four' because we are certain of the lie of one, for one person cannot be in two distant places at the same hour; nor does the judge know the truthful from the liar, so he is unable to judge due to contradiction or suspicion of lying; nor are the witnesses punished because each group completed the number of witnesses and truthfulness is possible. Second, that the two places are close with unity of time; then their testimony is permitted because it is possible that both events occurred at that time, since 'sunrise' refers to an extended period customarily, not specifically to the moment of its appearance from the horizon, and repetition of the act is possible. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And al-Hakim mentioned in his Kafi: If four testify against a man for zina and they differ regarding the woman, the place, or the time, their testimony is invalid unless their difference is regarding two close places, within a house or not, in which case the hadd is imposed by istihsan. End.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings when witnesses for zina disagree on the location of the act. The author presents two main scenarios. In the first, two witnesses say the zina occurred in Kufa and two in Basra; here, no hadd is imposed on the accused because each group does not constitute the required four witnesses for a single act, and the witnesses themselves are not punished for qadhf because there is a semblance of consistency (shubhat al-ittihad) due to the same woman and form of accusation. This differs from Zufar. In the second scenario, full four witnesses testify in each city. This splits into two subcases: (a) if the two places are distant but the time is exactly the same, impossibility of simultaneous presence confirms falsehood, so no hadd; (b) if places are close and time same, testimony is accepted by istihsan because the time may be considered extended and repetition is possible. Al-Hakim's Kafi supports this, adding that disagreement on the woman, place, or time invalidates testimony unless places are close, in which case istihsan applies. The Hanafi position is that close proximity allows reconciliation of testimonies through possibility of movement or repetition.

Key Terms
زنا (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse requiring four witnesses.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court, for zina requiring four witnesses.
نصاب الشهادة (nisab al-shahada): The required number of witnesses to prove a claim; for zina, four.
شبهة الاتحاد (shubhat al-ittihad): Semblance of unity; a legal doubt that arises when different testimonies share enough common elements to suggest they refer to the same act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario (two witnesses in Kufa, two in Basra), why are the witnesses not punished for qadhf according to the Hanafi majority?
A) Because the nisab is complete in each location.
B) Because the witness testimonies are identical.
C) Because there is a shubhat al-ittihad due to the same woman and form of accusation.
D) Because the judge is unable to decide.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school reconciles contradictory witness testimonies in zina by applying shubhat al-ittihad and istihsan, avoiding punishment of witnesses while preserving the hadd when possible.

Disagreement in One House: Istihsan Application
Ruling when witnesses disagree on exact location within one house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of istihsan to reconcile differing testimonies about location within a small house and distinguish when hadd is imposed or not.

Core Idea
Istihsan allows hadd when witnesses differ on the spot within one small house because reconciliation is possible.

When witnesses for zina give conflicting accounts of where the act occurred, does that invalidate their testimony? The answer depends on whether the location differences can be reconciled. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling that within a single small house, istihsan overrides strict qiyas, and both the man and woman are punished.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and apparent conflict
Two witnesses say zina occurred in one corner, two say another corner of the same house. The testimonies appear to differ on a material detail.
The house is small, not large.
2
Contrast qiyas vs. istihsan ruling
By qiyas (strict analogy to different cities), the real difference in place would prevent hadd. By istihsan, hadd is imposed because reconciliation is possible.
Istihsan is a Hanafi source of law that overrides qiyas for a stronger consideration.
3
Understand the basis of istihsan: reconciliation
The act could have started in one corner and ended in another due to movement, or witnesses perceived the same central act from different positions. This tawfiq (reconciliation) saves the testimony.
This only applies to small houses; a large house is like separate buildings.
4
Recognize the limitation: size matters
The rule is restricted to small houses. If the house is large (like a dar) or the witnesses refer to two separate houses, no hadd because reconciliation is impossible.
Two houses are like two cities.
5
Address the objection: coercion vs. willingness
A potential contradiction arises from Imam Abu Hanifa's stance on coercion: if witnesses differ on coercion vs. willingness, no hadd due to doubt, even though reconciliation is possible. The answer: coercion at the beginning negates hadd, so doubt prevents punishment, whereas different corners both equally require hadd.
This shows the nuance in applying istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو اختلفوا في بيت واحد حد الرجل والمرأة) أي اختلفوا في مكان الزنا من بيت واحد كما إذا شهد اثنان أنه زنى بها في زاوية منه واثنان أنه زنى بها في زاوية أخرى منه وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يجب لاختلاف المكان حقيقة. وجه الاستحسان أن التوفيق ممكن بأن يكون ابتداء الفعل في زاوية والانتهاء في زاوية أخرى بالاضطراب والحركة أو لأن الواقع في وسط البيت فيحسبه من في المقدم في المقدم ومن في المؤخر في المؤخر فيشهد بحسب ما عنده . أطلق في البيت وهو مقيد بالصغير لأن الكبير كالدار ولو اختلفا في دارين لا حد كالبلدين والحاصل أن الاختلاف في المكان مانع لقبولها إلا إذا أمكن التوفيق بأن يكون صغيراً. وقيد الاختلاف بما ذكر لأنهم لو اختلفوا في طولها وقصرها أو سمنها أو هزالها أو في لونها أو في ثيابها فإنه لا يمنع لإمكان التوفيق. وقد استشكل على هذا مذهب الإمام فيما إذا اختلفوا في الإكراه والطواعية فإن التوفيق فيه ممكن بأن يكون ابتداء الفعل كرهاً وانتهاؤه طواعية. قال في الكافي : يمكن أن يجاب عنه بأن ابتداء الفعل إذا كان عن إكراه لا يوجب الحد فبالنظر إلى الابتداء لا يجب وبالنظر إلى الانتهاء يجب فلا يجب بالشك، وهنا بالنظر إلى الزاويتين يجب فافترقا .
His saying: (And if they differed regarding one house, the man and woman are punished) meaning they differed regarding the place of zina within one house, such as if two witnessed that he committed zina with her in one corner and two witnessed that he committed zina with her in another corner. This is istihsan, and by qiyas it would not be required due to the real difference in place. The basis of istihsan is that reconciliation is possible, because the act could have begun in one corner and ended in another due to movement and motion, or because the act occurred in the middle of the house, so those in the front considered it in the front and those in the back considered it in the back, each testifying according to what he saw. He used the absolute term 'house' and it is restricted to a small house, because a large one is like a large building; and if they differ regarding two houses, there is no hadd, like two cities. The outcome is that difference in place prevents acceptance of testimony unless reconciliation is possible by the place being small. The difference is restricted to what was mentioned because if they differ regarding her height, shortness, fatness, thinness, color, or clothes, that does not prevent acceptance because reconciliation is possible. And an objection was raised against this regarding Imam Abu Hanifa's position when they differ on coercion vs. willingness, where reconciliation is possible—the act could begin under coercion and end willingly. It is said in al-Kafi: This can be answered by saying that if the beginning of the act is under coercion, it does not require hadd; so considering the beginning, it is not required, and considering the end, it is required, thus it is not required due to doubt. Here, considering the two corners, it is required, so they differ.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi ruling when witnesses for zina differ on the exact spot within a single house. The matn states that the man and woman are punished. While by qiyas (strict analogy) the difference in place would prevent hadd, istihsan allows it because the testimonies can be reconciled: the act may have started in one corner and ended in another, or witnesses may have perceived the same act from different positions. This applies only to small houses; a large house is like a separate building, and two houses are like two cities, where no hadd is imposed. The commentator notes that differences in physical attributes or clothing do not prevent testimony because they can be reconciled. A possible objection involves disagreement on coercion vs. willingness, but al-Kafi resolves it by noting that coercion at the start negates hadd, so the doubt prevents punishment, unlike the location difference where both corners equally require the hadd.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Legal preference to set aside qiyas for a stronger consideration, here the possibility of reconciliation.
توفيق (tawfiq): Reconciliation of apparently conflicting testimonies by a plausible explanation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when witnesses differ on the exact spot within a single small house, what is the ruling?
A) No hadd because the place differs.
B) Hadd is imposed by istihsan.
C) The witnesses are punished.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan permits imposing hadd when witnesses differ on location within a single small house because the testimonies can be reconciled through plausible movement or perspective.
