Three Cases Where Hadd Is Dropped: Virgin, Fasiq, and Testimony Upon Testimony
Three scenarios where hadd is dropped due to legal doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi cases where hadd is not imposed and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind each exception.

Core Idea
Hadd is dropped when a doubt (shubha) overrides the certainty of punishment.

The hadd penalties are serious, but the Hanafi school recognizes that certain circumstances create legal doubt that blocks their application. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three such scenarios: when the alleged victim is found to be a virgin, when the witnesses are sinful (fasiq), and when testimony is given through secondary witnesses. Understanding these exceptions clarifies how the Hanafi school balances textual punishments with principles of certainty and doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify each scenario
Read the passage and list the three distinct cases where the hadd is not imposed on anyone: (a) virgin woman, (b) fasiq witnesses, (c) testimony upon testimony.
2
Explain the reasoning for the virgin case
The passage states that a virgin woman's condition is incompatible with zina. The doubt arises from the evidence of her virginity, which can be established even by one woman's testimony. Because the accusation is clearly false, no hadd applies to either party.
This includes analogous cases like the man being a eunuch or the woman having a closed vagina.
3
Explain the reasoning for fasiq witnesses
Fasiq witnesses lack the required integrity (adala) to prove zina, so the hadd on the accused is not applied. However, their testimony still creates a semblance (shubha) of zina, which drops the hadd of qadhf from them. The passage contrasts this with murder, where qisas is not dropped by doubtful testimony.
This applies whether their sinfulness was known initially or discovered later.
4
Explain the reasoning for testimony upon testimony
Testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala shahada) introduces a double doubt: the possibility of falsehood in both the original and secondary witnesses. Therefore, it is not accepted in hudud, and neither set of witnesses is punished. If secondary witnesses are rejected, original witnesses cannot later testify again.
This rule is specific to hudud; in property cases, such testimony may be accepted.
5
Distinguish from property cases
The passage notes that in property matters, weak evidence (shubha) can establish rights, so testimony upon testimony may be accepted. Similarly, if rejection of witnesses was due to lack of eligibility (e.g., slavery), they can testify later after removal of the obstacle.
This highlights the higher evidentiary standard in hudud cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو شهدوا على زنا امرأة وهي بكر أو الشهود فسقه أو شهدوا على شهادة أربعة وإن شهد الأصول لم يحد أحد) بيان لثلاث مسائل لا حد فيها الأولى لو شهدوا على رجل أنه زنى بفلانة فوجدت فلانة بكراً بقول النساء لأن الزنا لا يتحقق مع بقاء البكارة فلا حد عليهما لظهور الكذب ولا على الشهود لأن سقوطه بقول النساء وشهادتهن حجة في إسقاط الحد وليس بحجة في إيجابه. وأشار المصنف إلى أنهم لو شهدوا على رجل بالزنا فوجد مجبوباً أو شهدوا عليها بالزنا فوجدت رتقاء أو قرناء فإنه لا حد على أحد لما ذكرنا. وأطلق في قوله "وهي بكر" فشمل ما إذا ثبتت بكارتها بقول امرأة واحدة وكذا في الرتق والقرن وكل ما يعمل فيه بقول النساء؛ كذا في كافي الحاكم. الثانية لو شهد أربعة فسقة بالزنا لاشتراط العدالة فلم يثبت الزنا فلا حد ولا حد على الشهود لأن الفاسق من أهل الأداء والتحمل وإن أدائه في نوع قصور لتهمة الفسق ولهذا لو قضى القاضي بشهادته ينفذ عندنا فيثبت بشهادتهم شبهة الزنا فسقط الحد عنهم. وأطلق في الفسقة فشمل ما إذا علم فسقهم في الابتداء أو ظهر فسقهم كما في الهداية. وأشار المصنف بسقوط الحد عن الشهود الفسقة إلى أن القاذف لو أقام أربعة من الفساق على أن المقذوف قد زنى يسقط عنه الحد ـ قالوا - بخلاف القاتل حيث لا يسقط عنه القتل بإقامة الشهود الفسقة على أن أولياء المقتول قد عفوا لأن وجوب القود بالقتل متيقن فلا يسقط عنه بالشك والاحتمال وحد القذف لم يجب بالقذف وإنما يجب بالعجز عن إقامة البيئة وتمامه في التبيين. الثالثة لو شهدوا على شهادة أربعة فلأن الشهادة على الشهادة لا تجوز في الحدود لما فيها من زيادة الشبهة لأن احتمال الكذب فيها في موضعين : في شهادة الأصول وفي شهادة الفروع ولا حد على الفروع لأن الحاكي للقذف لا يكون قاذفاً، وكذا لا حد على الأصول بالأولى فإذا شهد الفروع وردت شهادتهم ثم جاء الأصول بعد ذلك وشهدوا على معاينة ذلك الزنا بعينه لم تقبل شهادتهم ولم يحدوا أيضاً. المراد بقوله "وإن شهد الأصول لم يحد أحد" لأن شهادة الأصول قد ردت من وجه برد شهادة الفروع. قيد بالحد لأنه لو ردت شهادة الفروع في الأموال فإن شهادة الأصول بعده مقبولة لثبوت المال الشبهة دون الحد ولو ردت شهادة الأصول لم تقبل شهادة الأصول ولا مع الفروع بعده أبداً في كل شيء إن ردت لتهمة مع بقاء الأهلية، وإن ردت لعدم الأهلية كالعبيد والكفار تقبل شهادتهم في تلك الحادثة بعد العتق والإسلام لزوال المانع؛ كذا في التبيين
His saying: (And if they testify regarding a woman's zina while she is a virgin, or the witnesses are sinful, or they testify upon the testimony of four, and even if the original witnesses testify, no one is punished) is a statement of three issues in which there is no hadd: First, if they testify against a man that he committed zina with so-and-so, and so-and-so is found to be a virgin according to women's testimony, because zina cannot be verified while her hymen is intact, so there is no hadd on either due to apparent falsehood, nor on the witnesses because the negation of hadd is established by women's testimony, and their testimony is authoritative for dropping the hadd but not for establishing it. The author indicated that if they testify against a man for zina and he is found to be a eunuch, or they testify against a woman and she is found to be closed (ratqa') or having a horn (qarna'), there is no hadd on anyone for what we have mentioned. He used the absolute term 'while she is a virgin,' so it includes when her virginity is established by the statement of one woman, similarly for the closed and horned conditions and everything that is established by women's testimony; as in Kafi al-Hakim. Second, if four sinful people testify for zina, because righteousness is a condition, so zina is not proven, so there is no hadd, nor on the witnesses because a sinful person is among those who can perform and convey testimony, though their performance is somewhat deficient due to the suspicion of sin; thus if the judge rules based on their testimony, it is executed according to us, so their testimony establishes a semblance (shubha) of zina, so the hadd is dropped from them. He used the absolute term 'sinful' so it includes whether their sinfulness is known initially or appears later, as in al-Hidaya. The author indicated by dropping the hadd from sinful witnesses that if the accuser brings four sinful people that the accused committed zina, the hadd (of qadhf) is dropped from him. They said: contrary to the killer, where the death penalty is not dropped by bringing sinful witnesses that the heirs have forgiven, because the obligation of qisas by killing is certain, so it is not dropped by doubt and probability; whereas the hadd of qadhf is not established by the accusation itself, but rather by inability to bring evidence; and its completion is in al-Tabyin. Third, if they testify upon the testimony of four, because testimony upon testimony is not permitted in hudud due to the increased doubt, since the probability of falsehood exists in two places: in the testimony of the original witnesses and in the testimony of the secondary witnesses; nor is there hadd on the secondary witnesses because the narrator of qadhf is not a qadif; likewise, there is no hadd on the original witnesses even more so. If the secondary witnesses testify and their testimony is rejected, then later the original witnesses come and testify to eyewitnessing that same zina, their testimony is not accepted and they are not punished. What is meant by his saying 'even if the original witnesses testify, no one is punished' is that the testimony of the original witnesses has been rejected due to the rejection of the secondary witnesses' testimony. This is restricted to hudud because if the secondary witnesses' testimony is rejected in property cases, then the original witnesses' testimony afterwards is accepted because property is established by weak evidence unlike hudud; and if the original witnesses' testimony is rejected, then neither they nor the secondary witnesses are ever accepted afterwards in anything if the rejection was due to suspicion while eligibility remains; but if the rejection was due to lack of eligibility, like slaves or disbelievers, their testimony is accepted in that incident after emancipation or Islam because the obstacle has been removed; as in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three cases where no hadd is imposed on either the accused or the witnesses. First, if the woman is found to be a virgin (or the man a eunuch, or the woman with a closed vagina or horn), the testimony is clearly false, so no hadd. The virginity can be established by one woman's testimony. Second, if the witnesses are fasiq (sinful), their testimony is not sufficient to prove zina because they lack the required character; but they are not punished for qadhf because their testimony creates a semblance (shubha) of zina, which drops the hadd. This applies whether their sinfulness is known at the start or emerges later. A distinction is made with murder: in murder, the certainty of qisas prevents dropping it by doubtful testimony. Third, testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala shahada) is not accepted in hudud due to double doubt; neither the original nor secondary witnesses are punished. If secondary witnesses are rejected, later original witnesses cannot come anew because their testimony has already been undermined. However, in property cases, there is flexibility. If rejection was due to lack of eligibility (e.g., slavery or disbelief), later acceptance is possible once the obstacle is removed.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A virgin woman, whose hymen is intact, proving no recent intercourse.
فساق (fussaq): Sinful witnesses who lack legal integrity (adala) but can still create shubha.
شهادة على شهادة (shahada 'ala shahada): Testimony based on the testimony of original witnesses (secondary witnesses).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If four fasiq witnesses testify against a man for zina, what is the ruling?
A) The man is punished for zina.
B) The witnesses are punished for qadhf.
C) Neither the man nor the witnesses are punished.
D) Only the witnesses are punished.

Key Takeaway
Hadd is dropped in three cases of shubha: female virginity, fasiq witnesses, and secondary testimony.

Ineligible Witnesses in Zina Cases: Blind, Hadd-Punished, or Less than Four
Ruling on ineligible witnesses in zina cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ineligible witnesses (blind, hadd-punished, or fewer than four) in zina cases are punished for qadhf, and explain the qiyas basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
Ineligible witnesses create no doubt; they become slanderers liable for hadd.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author examines a scenario where the alleged witnesses of zina are themselves legally disqualified: blind persons, those who have been subjected to a hadd punishment, or a group of only three witnesses. The Hanafi ruling is clear: such witnesses do not merely have their testimony rejected; they are punished with the hadd of qadhf (false accusation) because their statements cannot even establish the shubha (doubt) necessary to avoid punishment. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning by analogy (qiyas) from property law to hadd cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being judged (ineligible testimony) and the legal consequence (witnesses receive hadd of qadhf).
The ruling applies to any witness who is blind, hadd-punished, or part of a group of fewer than four.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage uses qiyas: since property rights are not established by the testimony of blind or hadd-punished individuals, how can hadd (which requires even stricter proof) be established?
The unstated premise is that a witness must be eligible (ahl al-adāʾ) to create any legal effect.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is the lack of eligibility for testimony. Without eligibility, their claim carries no legal weight, so they are slanderers.
This analogy (qiyas) operates on the principle that the lesser (property) implies the greater (hadd).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may consider blind or hadd-punished persons capable of creating some doubt (shubha) in certain contexts, thus differing on punishment.
The Hanafi school holds firmly that such individuals are not from ahl al-shahada.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi within the school, derived from zahir al-riwayah. The applied ruling is that ineligible witnesses are punished.
This reflects the strict evidentiary standards for hudud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو كانوا عمياناً أو محدودين أو ثلاثة حد الشهود لا المشهود عليهما) لأنه لا يثبت بشهادة الأعمى والمحدود المال فكيف يثبت الحد وهم ليسوا من أهل أداء الشهادة فلم تثبت شبهة الزنا فكانوا قذفة فيحدون ومراده من ليس أهلاً للأداء فدخل العبد مع أنه ليس
His saying: (And if they are blind, or had been punished with hadd, or are three, the witnesses are punished but not the accused) because property rights are not established by the testimony of a blind person or one who has been punished with hadd, so how can hadd be established? And they are not among those eligible to give testimony, so no semblance of zina is established, thus they are considered slanderers and are punished. His intent is anyone not eligible for performance, so it includes a slave, even though he is not
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses cases where the witnesses are inherently ineligible to testify in zina cases: blind persons, those who have themselves been punished with hadd (e.g., for qadhf), or only three witnesses. In such cases, no shubha (semblance) of zina is established because these individuals are not fit to give testimony at all (unlike fasiq witnesses who can at least create doubt). Therefore, they are treated as mere slanderers (qadifa) and are punished with the hadd of qadhf, while the accused go free. The text also indicates that this includes a slave, as slaves are not eligible to testify. This ruling contrasts with the previous lesson where fasiq witnesses escaped punishment because their testimony created a doubt.

Key Terms
أعمى (a'ma): A blind person, who cannot testify in hudud because they cannot have witnessed the act.
محدود (mahdud): A person who has been subjected to a hadd punishment (e.g., for zina or qadhf), disqualified from testimony.
شبهة (shubha): A semblance or doubt that can prevent the imposition of hadd on the accuser.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The man is punished for zina.
B) The witnesses are punished for qadhf.
C) Both are punished.
D) Neither is punished.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who are blind, hadd-punished, or fewer than four cannot create shubha in zina cases; they are liable for qadhf.

No Hadd When Woman Is Found Virgin After Zina Testimony
First of three cases where no hadd is imposed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no hadd is imposed when a woman is found virgin after zina testimony, explain the proof based on women's testimony for isqat, and apply the same ruling to analogous cases (majbub, ratqa, qarna).

Core Idea
Zina is impossible if virginity is intact — women's testimony drops the hadd for accusers.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific scenario: after four witnesses testify to zina, the woman is found to be a virgin. The commentator explains that no hadd is imposed on any party because the testimony is manifestly false and the women's examination, accepted for dropping hadd, prevents punishment of the witnesses. This introduces the Hanafi principle that women's testimony is accepted for isqat (dropping) but not for ijab (establishing) a hadd penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with four witnesses testifying against a man and woman for zina, but the woman is found to be a virgin by women's examination. The ruling is: no hadd is imposed on the accused or the witnesses.
The hadd here refers to both the zina hadd and the qadhf hadd.
2
Locate the underlying principle
The ruling is based on the principle 'Shahadat al-nisa hujja fi isqat al-hadd wa laysa bi hujja fi ijabih' — women's testimony is evidence for dropping the hadd but not for establishing it.
This principle is derived from ijma within the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the logical link
Since the women's testimony establishes virginity, zina is physically impossible. Hence the accusation is false. The accused are innocent, and the accusers would normally be liable for qadhf, but the women's testimony that disproves zina also drops the hadd of qadhf from them.
The dropping of hadd from witnesses is a direct application of the isqat principle.
4
Extend to analogous cases
The same ruling applies if the man is found impotent (majbub) or the woman has a closed/obstructed genital tract (ratqa or qarna) — any physical impediment that makes zina impossible.
These cases are explicitly mentioned in the passage.
5
Note the evidentiary nuance
The passage notes that even a single woman's testimony suffices for establishing these physical conditions, as these are matters known only to women. The ruling applies broadly.
This is based on 'Kafi al-Hakim' and standard Hanafi practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو) شهدوا على زنا امرأة وهي بكر أو الشهود فسقه أو شهدوا على شهادة أربعة وإن شهد الأصول لم يحد أحد بيان لثلاث مسائل لا حد فيها الأولى لو شهدوا على رجل أنه زنى بفلانة فوجدت فلانة بكراً بقول النساء لأن الزنا لا يتحقق مع بقاء البكارة فلا حد عليهما لظهور الكذب ولا على الشهود لأن سقوطه بقول النساء وشهادتهن حجة في إسقاط الحد وليس بحجة في إيجابه. وأشار المصنف إلى أنهم لو شهدوا على رجل بالزنا فوجد مجبوباً أو شهدوا عليها بالزنا فوجدت رتقاء أو قرناء فإنه لا حد على أحد لما ذكرنا. وأطلق في قوله وهي بكر» فشمل ما إذا ثبتت بكارتها بقول امرأة واحدة وكذا في الرتق والقرن وكل ما يعمل فيه بقول النساء ; كذا في كافي الحاكم .
His statement: (And if) they testify about a man's zina with a woman, and she is a virgin, or the witnesses are sinful, or they testify on the testimony of four, and if the original witnesses testify, no one is flogged. Explanation of three issues in which there is no hadd. The first: if they testify against a man that he committed zina with so-and-so, and she is found to be a virgin according to the statement of women, because zina cannot be confirmed with the presence of virginity, so there is no hadd on them due to the apparent falsehood, and no hadd on the witnesses because its removal is by the statement of women, and their testimony is evidence for dropping the hadd but not for establishing it. And the author indicated that if they testify about a man committing zina and he is found to be impotent, or they testify about a woman and she is found to have a closed vulva or fused labia, then there is no hadd on anyone for what we mentioned. And he said broadly 'and she is a virgin' to include if her virginity is established by the statement of a single woman, and likewise regarding the closed vulva and fused labia, and everything that is determined by the statement of women. This is in the Kafi of al-Hakam.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn discussing three scenarios where no hadd is imposed. The first scenario: four witnesses testify that a man committed zina with a specific woman. Upon investigation, the woman is found to be a virgin according to the examination of women. Since zina cannot physically occur while the hymen remains intact, the testimony is clearly false. Therefore, no hadd is imposed on the accused man or woman because the falsehood is apparent. Additionally, no hadd is imposed on the witnesses, even though they falsely accused, because the hadd of qadhf is dropped by the women's testimony. In Hanafi law, women's testimony is accepted as evidence for dropping a hadd (isqat al-hadd) but not for establishing one. The author extends the same ruling to analogous cases: if the man is found to be impotent (majbub), or the woman is found to have a closed vulva (ratqa) or fused labia (qarna), the hadd is similarly dropped. Furthermore, the ruling applies even if the woman's condition is established by the word of a single woman, as this is a matter known only to women. The ruling is standard Hanafi and is found in the authoritative works.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A woman who has not had sexual intercourse; her hymen is intact.
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose male organ is cut off or fully disabled, making him impotent.
رتقاء (ratqa): A woman whose vagina is closed or blocked, preventing intercourse.
قرناء (qarna): A woman whose labia are fused or have a fleshy growth obstructing intercourse.
شهادة النساء (shahadat al-nisa): The testimony of women, which in Hanafi law is accepted in matters of the body that men do not know, such as virginity, for dropping hadd but not for establishing it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are punished with hadd al-qadhf.
B) They are not punished because women's testimony drops the hadd.
C) They are punished because the woman is a virgin.
D) They are not punished because the man confessed.

Key Takeaway
When a woman is found virgin after zina testimony, no hadd is imposed on anyone because the testimony is false and the women's testimony drops the hadd from the accusers.

No Hadd with Fasiq Witnesses in Zina Testimony
Ruling with proof on fasiq witnesses in zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when four fasiq witnesses testify for zina and explain why no hadd is imposed on the accused or the witnesses.

Core Idea
Fasiq testimony creates a shubha that repels hadd, even though it doesn't prove zina.

In Hanafi law, the testimony of upright ('adil) witnesses is a strict requirement for establishing zina. But what happens when the witnesses are fasiq (sinful)? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the second case where no hadd is imposed: the accused escapes the hadd because the condition of 'adala is not met, and the witnesses escape the hadd of qadhf because their testimony, though deficient, creates a doubt (shubha) about their accusation. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case
Recognize that the scenario involves four fasiq witnesses testifying to zina. The condition of 'adala (uprightness) is not satisfied, so the central act (zina) is not legally established.
The absence of 'adala means the testimony is not sufficient to prove zina.
2
Determine the Ruling on the Accused
Since zina is not proven, the accused cannot be subjected to the hadd punishment for zina. The hadd is therefore dropped.
3
Determine the Ruling on the Witnesses
The witnesses are not punished with hadd al-qadhf (false accusation) because their testimony, though flawed, creates a shubha (doubt) that the accusation might be true. The Hanafi principle that a fasiq is still ahl al-ada' wa al-tahammul allows his testimony to create this shubha.
Shubha repels the hadd, even if the testimony is not fully probative.
4
Understand the Scope of Fasiq
The ruling applies whether the witnesses' fasiq status is known at the time of testimony or is discovered later. The doubt is effective in both cases.
This broadens the protection for the witnesses.
5
Contrast with the Murder Case
In murder, bringing fasiq witnesses to claim the heirs pardoned does not drop the qisas. The obligation for qisas is certain, unlike the hadd of qadhf which arises only due to lack of evidence.
The certainty of the obligation (qisas) prevents shubha from repelling it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية لو شهد أربعة فسقة بالزنا لاشتراط العدالة فلم يثبت الزنا فلا حد ولا حد على الشهود لأن الفاسق من أهل الأداء والتحمل وإن أدائه في نوع قصور لتهمة الفسق ولهذا لو قضى القاضي بشهادته ينفذ عندنا فيثبت بشهادتهم شبهة الزنا فسقط الحد عنهم. وأطلق في الفسقة فشمل ما إذا علم فسقهم في الابتداء أو ظهر فسقهم كما في الهداية. وأشار المصنف بسقوط الحد عن الشهود الفسقة إلى أن القاذف لو أقام أربعة من الفساق على أن المقذوف قد زنى يسقط عنه الحد ـ قالوا - بخلاف القاتل حيث لا يسقط عنه القتل بإقامة الشهود الفسقة على أن أولياء المقتول قد عفوا لأن وجوب القود بالقتل متيقن فلا يسقط عنه بالشك والاحتمال وحد القذف لم يجب بالقذف وإنما يجب بالعجز عن إقامة البيئة وتمامه في التبيين.
The second: if four sinful people testify about zina, because uprightness ('adala) is a condition, so zina is not established, so there is no hadd, and no hadd on the witnesses because the sinful person is among those capable of bearing and transmitting testimony, although his performance is somewhat deficient due to the suspicion of sinfulness. For this reason, if the judge passes judgment based on their testimony, it is executed according to us, and thus a doubt of zina is established by their testimony, so the hadd is dropped from them. And he broadened the term 'fasiq' to include whether their sinfulness is known from the beginning or becomes apparent later, as in al-Hidayah. And the author indicated by the dropping of hadd from the sinful witnesses that if an accuser (qadhif) brings four sinful witnesses that the accused committed zina, the hadd drops from him. They said: contrary to the murderer, where he is not saved from execution by bringing sinful witnesses that the heirs had pardoned, because the obligation of qisas for murder is certain, so it is not dropped by doubt and probability, and the hadd of qadhf is not obligatory by the accusation, but rather by the inability to produce evidence. The completion is in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains the second case where no hadd is imposed. Four witnesses who are fasiq (sinners, not upright) testify against someone for zina. Since 'adala (uprightness) is a condition for the acceptance of testimony in hudud, their testimony does not establish zina. Therefore, no hadd is imposed on the accused. Additionally, no hadd of qadhf is imposed on these witnesses themselves, even though they made an accusation that would normally require punishment. The reason is that a fasiq person is still capable of bearing and transmitting testimony (ahl al-ada' wa al-tahammul), but his performance is deficient due to the suspicion of sin. However, this deficiency is not total; if a judge inadvertently passes judgment based on their testimony, the judgment is executed in Hanafi law. This creates a doubt (shubha) that the accusation was true, and doubts repel hadd punishments. Therefore, the hadd is dropped from the witnesses. The author notes that this applies whether the fasiq status was known initially or discovered later. The text also contrasts this with a murder case: if someone kills and brings fasiq witnesses to claim that the heirs pardoned, this does not save him from qisas because the obligation of qisas is established with certainty, unlike the hadd of qadhf which becomes obligatory only due to inability to produce evidence.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking the required 'adala for testimony.
عدالة ('adala): Uprightness and moral integrity, a condition for the acceptance of testimony in hudud and other matters.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason the hadd is not imposed on the fasiq witnesses in the zina case?
A) Because they are not legally capable of giving testimony.
B) Because their testimony creates a doubt (shubha) that repels the hadd.
C) Because the accused confessed.
D) Because the judge nullified the testimony.

Key Takeaway
Fasiq testimony in zina creates a doubt (shubha) that repels both the hadd on the accused and the hadd of qadhf on the witnesses.

Substitute Testimony Invalid in Hudud
Explaining the third case where no hadd is imposed due to substitute testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on shahada ala shahada in hudud, explain why it is not accepted, and apply the consequences when original witnesses testify after their substitutes are rejected.

Core Idea
Substitute testimony is invalid in hudud because it multiplies doubt, and hudud are repelled by doubts.

In this passage from Bahr al-Raiq, the author discusses the third case in which no hadd is imposed: when witnesses testify based on the testimony of others. This is known as shahada ala shahada, or substitute testimony. The ruling has significant implications for both original and substitute witnesses, and it distinguishes hudud from property cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act being ruled upon is substitute testimony (shahada ala shahada) in hudud cases. The ruling is that it is not accepted, meaning no hadd is imposed based on it.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the reason (ta'lil) given: 'because it increases doubt (shubha)' and hudud are repelled by doubts. This is based on ijma of Hanafi fuqaha.
3
Trace the consequences
If substitute witnesses (furu') testify and are rejected, and then the original witnesses (usul) come later to testify directly, their testimony is also rejected because the entire matter is tainted by doubt. No one is flogged.
4
Distinguish from property cases
In property cases, substitute testimony is accepted because property can be established by preponderance of doubt. The text explicitly contrasts this: 'ثبوت المال الشبهة دون الحد'.
5
Note the exception for eligibility
If the rejection was due to lack of eligibility (e.g., slave or kafir), testimony can be accepted after the impediment is removed (emancipation or Islam). This is different from rejection due to suspicion with eligibility remaining, which is permanent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثة لو شهدوا على شهادة أربعة فلأن الشهادة على الشهادة لا تجوز في الحدود لما فيها من زيادة الشبهة لأن احتمال الكذب فيها في موضعين : في شهادة الأصول وفي شهادة الفروع ولا حد على الفروع لأن الحاكي للقذف لا يكون قاذفاً، وكذا لا حد على الأصول بالأولى فإذا شهد الفروع وردت شهادتهم ثم جاء الأصول بعد ذلك وشهدوا على معاينة ذلك الزنا بعينه لم تقبل شهادتهم ولم يحدوا أيضاً. المراد بقوله «وإن شهد الأصول لم يحد أحد لأن شهادة الأصول قد ردت من وجه برد شهادة الفروع . قيد بالحد لأنه لو ردت شهادة الفروع في الأموال فإن شهادة الأصول بعده مقبولة لثبوت المال الشبهة دون الحد ولو ردت شهادة الأصول لم تقبل شهادة الأصول ولا مع الفروع بعده أبداً في كل شيء إن ردت لتهمة مع بقاء الأهلية، وإن ردت لعدم الأهلية كالعبيد والكفار تقبل شهادتهم في تلك الحادثة بعد العتق والإسلام لزوال المانع؛ كذا في التبيين.
The third: if they testify on the testimony of four, because testimony on testimony is not permissible in hudud due to the increase of doubt, because the possibility of falsehood exists in two places: in the testimony of the originals and in the testimony of the branches. And there is no hadd on the branches because the reporter of a slander is not a slanderer. Likewise, there is no hadd on the originals a fortiori. So if the branches testify and their testimony is rejected, then the originals come afterward and testify to the very sighting of that zina, their testimony is not accepted, and they are not flogged either. The meaning of his statement 'And if the originals testify, no one is flogged' is because the testimony of the originals has been rejected indirectly by the rejection of the branches' testimony. He restricted it to hadd because if the branches' testimony is rejected in property matters, then the originals' testimony afterwards is accepted because property is established by doubt, unlike hadd. And if the originals' testimony is rejected, their testimony is not accepted, nor with the branches afterwards ever in anything if the rejection is due to suspicion while eligibility remains. But if the rejection is due to lack of eligibility, like slaves and disbelievers, their testimony is accepted in that incident after emancipation and Islam because the impediment is removed; this is in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains the third case where no hadd is imposed: when witnesses testify based on the testimony of others (shahada ala shahada, or substitute testimony). This type of testimony is not accepted in hudud because it increases the possibility of falsehood: the error could be in the original witnesses or in the substitute witnesses. Therefore, no hadd is imposed on either: the substitutes are not punished because they are merely reporting the slander, not originating it; the originals are a fortiori not punished because their testimony was not the basis of the rejection. If the substitutes testify first and are rejected, and then the originals come to testify to the same event directly, their testimony is also not accepted because it is as if the entire testimony was rejected. This is specific to hudud; in property cases, such a situation might allow acceptance due to the general principle that property can be established by doubt. The author also distinguishes between rejection due to suspicion (tuhma) while eligibility remains (in which case the originals' testimony is permanently rejected) and rejection due to lack of eligibility (like being a slave or kafir), in which case the witness can testify again after the impediment is removed.

Key Terms
الشهادة على الشهادة (al-shahada 'ala al-shahada): Substitute testimony, where a witness testifies based on the testimony of another witness, not on personal observation.
الأصول (al-usul): The original witnesses who directly observed the act.
الفروع (al-furu'): The substitute witnesses who testify based on the testimony of the originals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is testimony on testimony (shahada ala shahada) not accepted in hudud?
A) Because it is not permissible in any area of law.
B) Because it increases the possibility of falsehood.
C) Because the Quran explicitly forbids it.
D) Because it requires four witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Substitute testimony is not accepted in hudud because it multiplies doubt, and hudud are repelled by any doubt.

intermediate
6 min
Witnesses Who Are Blind, Muhaddid, or Less Than Four Are Punished
Ruling with proof on disqualification of qadhf witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witnesses who are blind, muhaddid, or less than four in qadhf cases and identify the proof from 'Umar's action.

Core Idea
Disqualified witnesses become slanderers and face hadd al-qadhf themselves.

In Hanafi fiqh, testifying to zina is a serious matter. If the witnesses themselves are legally disqualified—whether due to blindness, a previous hadd punishment, or insufficient number—the presumption of valid testimony collapses. They are then treated as slanderers and punished with 80 lashes. This lesson explores the rationale and the proof from the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of disqualified witnesses
List the three types mentioned: blind (a'ma), those already punished for qadhf (muhaddid), and fewer than four witnesses.
2
Explain why each category disqualifies
Blind witnesses cannot see the act; muhaddid have lost credibility in hudud; fewer than four means the testimony is not a complete legal proof.
3
Determine the ruling on these witnesses
The witnesses themselves are punished with hadd al-qadhf (80 lashes), not the accused.
They are considered qadhaft (slanderers).
4
Analyze the proof from 'Umar's action
'Umar flogged three witnesses against al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba with silent approval of the Companions, establishing the ruling as ijma.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi with ijma sukuti.
5
Apply the ruling consistently
The ruling applies whether all or only some witnesses are disqualified, and includes slaves who are also ineligible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو كانوا عمياناً أو محدودين أو ثلاثة حد الشهود لا المشهود عليهما) لأنه لا يثبت بشهادة الأعمى والمحدود المال فكيف يثبت الحد وهم ليسوا من أهل أداء الشهادة فلم تثبت شبهة الزنا فكانوا قذفة فيحدون ومراده من ليس أهلاً للأداء فدخل العبد مع أنه ليس بأهل للتحمل أيضاً، ولا فرق بين أن يكون الكل كذلك أو بعضهم كذلك، وأما إذا نقص عددهم عن الأربعة فلأنهم قذفة لأن الشهادة قذف حقيقة وخروجها عنه باعتبار الحسبة ولا حسبة عند النقصان وحد عمر رضي الله عنه الثلاثة الذين شهدوا على المغيرة بن شعبة بمحضر من الصحابة رضي الله عنهم من غير نكير .
His statement: (And if they are blind, or have been previously punished with hadd, or three) the witnesses are flogged, not the accused, because property is not established by the testimony of a blind person or one who has received hadd, so how can hadd be established? And they are not among the people eligible to give testimony, so no doubt of zina is established, so they are slanderers and are flogged. And he intended by 'not eligible to give testimony' anyone not eligible, so that includes the slave, even though he is also not eligible to bear testimony. There is no difference whether all are like that or some of them. As for when their number is less than four, they are slanderers because testimony is essentially slander, and it only exits that category by being a valid legal testimony (hissba), and there is no hissba when the number is deficient, and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, flogged the three who testified against al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba in the presence of the Companions, without any denial.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage discusses witnesses who are not legally qualified to testify in hudud cases. The rule is: if the witnesses are blind, or have themselves been punished with hadd al-qadhf (muhaddid), or their number is less than four, then the witnesses themselves are punished with hadd al-qadhf, while the accused are not punished. The reason: these witnesses are not considered 'ahl al-ada' (those capable of giving accepted testimony). For example, the testimony of a blind person is not accepted even in property cases, let alone hudud. Similarly, a person who has been punished for qadhf cannot be a witness in hudud. Their testimony does not create any shubha (doubt) that could repel the hadd from them, so they are treated as ordinary slanderers (qadhaft) and are flogged (80 lashes). The author also includes the slave in this category because a slave is not eligible to bear testimony (tahammul) or give testimony (ada') in hudud. It makes no difference whether all the witnesses are disqualified or only some. The deficiency in number (less than four) also means the testimony is not a valid legal testimony (hissba), so the witnesses are slanderers. This was the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, who flogged three witnesses who testified against al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba, and the Companions did not object.

Key Terms
أعمى (a'ma): A blind person whose testimony is not accepted in matters requiring sight, including hudud.
محدود (muhaddid): A person who has been punished with hadd al-qadhf; their testimony is not accepted in hudud.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; the hadd punishment is 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Three witnesses testify that a man committed zina. What is the ruling on these witnesses according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) They are not punished because they are witnesses.
B) They are punished with hadd al-qadhf.
C) They are punished but the accused is also punished.
D) They are given ta'zir punishment.

Key Takeaway
In Hudud, witnesses who are legally disqualified become slanderers themselves and face hadd al-qadhf.
